    　　少阳司天，心痛胃脘痛，厥逆鬲不通，其主暴速。　　 【注　心痛烦心者，心包络所生病也。胃脘痛者，木克土也。土位中央，中鬲不通，则上下厥逆也。风气迅速，故主暴速。】　　太阳司天，水饮内禾　畜，中满不食。　　 【注　水湿之为病也。】

    　　　　　六元正纪大论

    　　太阳司天之政，二之气，民病气郁中满。　　 【注　阳气郁遏于内也。】
    　　木郁之发，民病胃脘当心而痛，上支两胁，鬲咽不通，食饮不下。　　 【注　木盛而土伤也。】
    　　太阴所至，为积饮否隔。
    　　 【注　此春病之常也。】
    　　太阴所至，为中满霍乱吐下。
    　　 【注　此秋病之常也。】

    　　　　灵枢经

    　　　　　邪气脏腑病形篇

    　　脾脉微急为膈中，食饮入而还出，后沃沫。　　 【注　脾有寒不能运化饮食，故为膈中。脾不能游溢津液，上归于肺，四布于皮毛，故涎沫之从口出也。】[6p]

    In the realm governed by Lesser Yang, there are heart pain and stomach pain, with counterflow and obstruction in the diaphragm, signifying rapid occurrences. [Note: Heart pain arises from disorders of the pericardium. Stomach pain results from the wood element overcoming the earth. The earth, located centrally, does not flow through; thus, there is counterflow above and below. The swift nature of wind energy is why it signifies rapid occurrences.]

    In the realm governed by Greater Yang, water and drink are trapped within, causing fullness and lack of appetite. [Note: This refers to diseases caused by water and humidity.]

    The Great Discussion on the Six Elements

    The governance of Greater Yang results in two energies, causing the people to suffer from internal stagnation. [Note: Yang energy is confined within.] When wood is stagnated, people suffer from stomach pain, engendered by the heart and upper side, with obstruction in the diaphragm and inability to consume food and drink. [Note: The abundance of wood injures the earth.]

    When the influence of Greater Yin arrives, it causes accumulated fluids to be trapped. [Note: This is a common ailment in spring.] When the influence of Greater Yin arrives, it leads to fullness, chaos, vomiting, and diarrhea. [Note: This is a common ailment in autumn.]

    The Canon of the Spiritual Pivot

    On the Manifestations of Pathogenic Qi in the Organs and Bowels

    A frail and rapid pulse in the spleen indicates obstruction in the diaphragm, where food and drink enter and then exit, followed by regurgitation. [Note: The spleen is cold and unable to transform food and drink, hence the obstruction in the diaphragm. The spleen is unable to distribute the fluids back to the lungs and outward to the skin and hair, hence the spittle emerging from the mouth.][6p]

    　　　　　本神篇

    　　愁忧者，气闭塞而不行。
    　　 【注　伤其心脏之神气也。】

    　　　　　终始篇

    　　人迎四盛，且大且数，名曰溢阳，溢阳为外格。脉口四盛，且大且数者，名曰溢阴，溢阴为内关。内关不通，死不治。人迎与太阴脉口俱盛四倍以上，命曰关格。关格者，与之短期。　　 【注　外格者，谓阳盛于外而无阴气之和；内关者，阴盛于内而无阳气之和。关格者，阴关于内，阳格于外也，是为关阴格阳之死候矣。】　　人迎与脉口俱盛三倍以上，命曰阴阳俱溢。如是者不开，则血脉闭塞，气无所行，流淫于中，五脏内伤。如此者因而炙之，则变易而为他病矣。　　 【注　人迎与脉口俱盛，命曰阴阳俱溢。盖阴盛于内则阳盛于外，阳盛于左则阴盛于右矣。若不以针开之，则血脉闭塞，气无所行，流溢于中，则内伤五脏矣。】[7p]

    The Spirit of the Divine

    Those who are troubled and anxious have their qi obstructed and unable to flow.
    【Note: This refers to the injury to the spirit and qi of the heart.】

    The Beginning and End

    The Renying pulse is strong and frequent, known as the Overflowing Yang, and the Overflowing Yang represents the external aspect. The pulse at the Yuankou is strong and frequent, known as the Overflowing Yin, and the Overflowing Yin represents the internal aspect. If the internal aspect is not unblocked, it leads to death without treatment. If the Renying and the Taiyin pulse are both significantly strong (four times or more), it is referred to as the Closed Barrier. The Closed Barrier indicates a short timeframe for survival.
    【Note: The external aspect refers to excessive Yang without the balancing Yin; the internal aspect represents excessive Yin without the balancing Yang. The Closed Barrier reflects Yin within and Yang obstructed outside, indicating the condition where internal Yin fails to harmonize with external Yang, signaling imminent death.】 If the Renying and the pulse at the Yuankou are both excessively strong (three times or more), it is referred to as both Yin and Yang overflowing. If not unblocked in such cases, the blood vessels become obstructed, the qi cannot flow, and it stagnates within, harming the five organs. If one applies heat treatment in such circumstances, it will change into another disease.
    【Note: When both the Renying and the pulse at the Yuankou are strong, it is termed both Yin and Yang overflowing. Essentially, if Yin is excessive internally, then Yang must be excessive externally, and if Yang is excessive on the left, then Yin will be excessive on the right. If needles are not used to unblock the qi, the blood vessels will close up, qi will stagnate, resulting in damage to the five organs.】[7p]

    　　　　　脉度篇

    　　五脏不和则七窍不通，六腑不和则留为痈。故邪在腑则阳脉不和，阳脉不和则气留之，气留之则阳气盛矣。阳气太盛则阴脉不利，阴脉不利则血留之，血留之则阴气盛矣。阴气太盛则阳气不能荣也，故曰关。阳气太盛则阴气弗能荣也，故曰格。阴阳俱盛，不能相荣，故曰关格。关格者，不得尽期而死也。　　 【注　关谓关阴于内，格谓格阳于外，如是则阴阳俱盛，不得相荣，故曰关格者，不得尽期而死也。】
    　　　　〗　/P>

    　　人迎四倍者，且大且数，名曰溢阳。溢阳为外格，死不治。必审按其本末，察其寒热，以验其脏腑之病。　　 【注　溢阳者，阳盛之气溢于脉中，气血之相合也。】　　寸口四倍者，名曰内关。内关者且大且数，死不治。必审按其本末之寒温，以验其脏腑之病。[8p]

    Pulse Diagnosis

    When the five organs are not harmonious, the seven orifices do not function; when the six bowels are not harmonious, abscesses arise. Therefore, if the evils reside in the bowels, the yang vessels are unbalanced; if the yang vessels are unbalanced, qi is retained; if qi is retained, yang energy becomes excessive. When yang energy is excessive, the yin vessels are impaired; if the yin vessels are impaired, blood is retained; if blood is retained, yin energy becomes excessive. When yin energy is excessive, yang energy cannot nourish; hence it is called “closure.” When yang energy is excessive, yin energy cannot nourish; hence it is called “stagnation.” When both yin and yang are excessive, they cannot support each other, so it is called “closure and stagnation.” Those in the state of closure and stagnation cannot die at their appointed time. [Note: "Closure" refers to closure of the yin internally, and "stagnation" to obstruction of the yang externally. In such a state, both yin and yang are excessive and cannot nourish each other, hence it is called closure and stagnation, leading to death before its appointed time.]

    When the pulse at the person’s external gate is fourfold, both large and rapid, it is called "overflowing yang." Overflowing yang represents external stagnation, indicating death without remedy. One must carefully examine its origin and result, check its coldness and heat, to confirm the diseases of the organs. [Note: Overflowing yang refers to the overwhelming presence of yang qi within the vessels, resulting from the combination of qi and blood.] When the pulse at the inch (cun) position is fourfold, it is termed "internal closure." Internal closure also presents as large and rapid, indicating death without remedy. One must carefully examine its origins in temperature to confirm the diseases of the organs.[8p]

    　　　　　上膈篇

    　　黄帝曰：气为上膈者，食饮入而还出，余已知之矣。虫为下膈，下膈者，食晬时乃出，余未得其意，愿卒闻之！岐伯曰：喜怒不适，食饮不节，寒温不时，则寒汁流于肠中，流于肠中则虫寒，虫寒则积聚，守于下管则肠胃充郭，卫气不营，邪气居之。人食则虫上食，虫上食则下管虚，下管虚则邪气胜之。积聚以留，留则痈成。痈成则下管约。其痈在管内者，即而痛深；其痈在外者，则痈外而痛浮，痈上皮热。　　【注　因于喜怒不适，食饮不节，寒温不时，病在膈上者食饮入而还出，病在膈下者食入晬时乃还。夫胃者，水谷血气之海也。因于外邪，致汁沫渗留于肠外，不得散则日以成积。如因于内伤，汁沫留于肠内，则渐渍而成痈。痈在脘内则痛而深，在外则痛浮，在痈上之皮必热。】[9p]

    The Upper Diaphragm Chapter

    The Yellow Emperor said: Qi is what constitutes the upper diaphragm, where food and drink enter and then return out. I have already understood this. The worm constitutes the lower diaphragm; the lower diaphragm releases food and drink at the appropriate time, but I have not yet grasped its meaning, and I wish to hear it completely! Qi Bo replied: When emotions are out of balance, when food and drink are irregular, and when temperatures are inappropriate, then cold juice flows within the intestines. When it flows within the intestines, the worms become cold; when the worms are cold, they accumulate. When they become lodged in the lower passage, the intestines and stomach are filled with stagnation, and the protective Qi fails to nourish, allowing evil Qi to dwell there. When a person eats, the worms consume the food. When the worms consume the food, the lower passage becomes deficient; when the lower passage is deficient, the evil Qi overcomes it. Stagnation persists, and if it remains, sores develop. When sores develop, the lower passage contracts. If the sore is inside the passage, it causes deep pain; if the sore is outside, it results in external swelling and superficial pain, with the skin over the sore being hot.

    [Note: This arises from emotional imbalance, irregularities in food and drink, and inappropriate temperature. If the illness is located in the upper diaphragm, food and drink will enter and return. If the illness is in the lower diaphragm, food will only return at the appropriate time. The stomach is the sea of water, grains, and blood Qi. When affected by external evils, juices and froths seep and remain outside the intestines; if they do not disperse, they accumulate over time. If due to internal injury, the juices and froths stay within the intestines, they gradually soak and form sores. Sores in the interior cause deep pain; those in the exterior cause superficial pain, and the skin over the sores must be hot.][9p]

    　　　　扁鹊难经

    　　　　　关格

    　　脉有太过，有不及，有阴阳相乘，有覆有溢，有关有格，何谓也？然。关之前者，阳之动也。脉当见九分见一寸而沉，过者法曰太过，减者法曰不及，遂入尺为覆，为内关外格，此阳乘之脉也。故曰覆溢是其真脏之脉，人不病而死也。　　经言气独行于五脏，不营于六腑者，何也？然。夫气之所行也，如水之流不得息也，故阴脉营于五脏，阳脉营于六腑，如环无端，莫知其纪，终而复始。其不覆溢，人气内温于脏腑，外濡于腠理。[10p]

    Bian Que's Difficult Classic

    Guan Ge

    The pulse can be too full, insufficient, have yin and yang intermingled, and can be excessive or deficient, related or unconnected—what does this mean? Indeed. The pulse before the guan (barrier) represents the movement of yang. The pulse should reveal nine parts and one inch to be deep; if it is excessive, it is called too full, if it is reduced, it is termed insufficient, thus entering the measurement scale as covering or unblocking, which reflects the yang pulse. Therefore, it is said that excess and overflow represent the true pulse of the organs, leading to death without illness. The classic says that qi exclusively circulates in the five organs, without engaging in the six bowels; why is that? Indeed. Qi flows as water does, without pause, hence the yin pulse nourishes the five organs while the yang pulse nourishes the six bowels, resembling a ring without end, where its course is unknown, ending and beginning anew. When there is no overflow, human qi remains warm in the organs and moist on the skin.[10p]

    　　　　金匮要略 【汉　张机】

    　　　　　胃反证治

    　　呕吐篇曰：问曰：病人脉数，数为热，当消谷引食而反吐者，何也？师曰：以发其汗，令阳微，膈气虚，脉乃数。数为客热，不能消谷，胃中虚冷故也。脉弦者虚也，胃气无余，朝食暮吐，变为胃反。寒在于上，医反下之，今脉反弦，故名曰虚。　　寸口脉微而数，微则无气，无气则荣虚，荣虚则血不足，血不足则胸中冷。　　趺阳脉浮而濇，浮则为虚，虚则伤脾，脾伤则不磨，朝食暮吐，暮食朝吐，宿谷不化，名曰胃反。脉紧而濇，其病难治。食已即吐者，大黄甘草汤主之。　　胃反呕吐者，大半夏汤主之。
    　　胃反吐而渴欲饮水者，茯苓泽泻汤主之。　　诸呕吐，谷不得下者，小半夏汤主之。
    　　　　中藏经 【汉　华佗】

    　　　　　阴阳否格论[11p]

    Golden Coffer Essentials [Han, Zhang Ji]

    Treatment for Stomach Reflux

    In the Vomiting chapter it says: A question was asked: If a patient has a rapid pulse, and the rapidity indicates heat, why do they vomit after consuming grains? The master replied: This is to induce sweating, leading to a slight yang, causing the diaphragm qi to be empty, resulting in a rapid pulse. The rapid pulse represents an external heat that cannot digest food, due to coolness and emptiness in the stomach. A wiry pulse indicates emptiness; the stomach qi is insufficient, leading to morning food being vomited in the evening, which is termed stomach reflux. Cold accumulates above, but the physician treats below, resulting in a wiry pulse, hence it is called empty. The pulse at the inch is thin and rapid; thin means no qi, no qi leads to a deficiency of nourishment, and deficiency of nourishment results in cold in the chest.

    The pulse at the foot yang is floating and slippery; floating indicates emptiness, and emptiness damages the spleen. Injury to the spleen does not digest food, leading to morning food being vomited in the evening or evening food in the morning, with undigested grains, termed stomach reflux. A tight and slippery pulse indicates a difficult condition to treat. If vomiting occurs immediately after eating, one should administer Da Huang Gan Cao Decoction. For those with stomach reflux and vomiting, Da Ban Xia Decoction is prescribed. For individuals with stomach reflux and thirst desiring water, Fu Ling Ze Xie Decoction is recommended. For all types of vomiting where grains cannot descend, Xiao Ban Xia Decoction should be used.

    Middle Storehouse Classic [Han, Hua Tuo]

    The Theory of Yin and Yang Dysfunction[11p]

    　　阳气上而不下，曰否；阴气下而不上，亦曰否。阳气下而不上，曰格；阴气上而不下，亦曰格。否格者，谓阴阳不相从也。阳奔于上则燔脾肺，其生疸也，其色黄赤，皆起于阳极也。阴走于下则冰肾肝，其生厥也，其色青黑，皆发于阴极也。疸为黄疸也，厥为寒厥也，由阴阳否格不通而生焉。阳燔则治以水，阴厥则助以火，乃阴阳相济之道耳。
    　　　　脉诀 【晋　王叔和】

    　　　　　脉法

    　　洪脉关前热在胸，到关翻胃几千重。
    　　　　千金方 【唐　孙思邈】

    　　　　　噎塞论

    　　《古今录验》云：五噎者，气忧劳食思也。气噎者，心悸上下不通，噎哕不彻，胸胁苦痛。忧噎者，天阴苦厥逆，心下悸动，手足逆冷。劳噎者，苦气膈，胁下支满，胸中填塞，令手足逆冷，不能自温。食噎者，食无多少，惟胸中苦塞常痛，不得喘息。思噎者，心悸动喜忘，目视(目巟)(目巟)。此皆忧恚嗔怒，寒气上入胸胁所致也。[12p]

    When yang energy rises but does not descend, it is called "negation"; when yin energy descends but does not rise, it is also called "negation." When yang energy descends but does not rise, it is called "stagnation"; when yin energy rises but does not descend, it is likewise called "stagnation." The terms negation and stagnation imply that yin and yang do not mutually support each other. When yang rushes upward, it scorches the spleen and lungs, leading to jaundice, characterized by yellow and red colors, all arising from the extreme of yang. When yin moves downward, it freezes the kidneys and liver, resulting in syncope, characterized by blue and black colors, all stemming from the extreme of yin. Jaundice pertains to yellow jaundice, and syncope refers to cold syncope, both arising from the obstruction of the interaction between yin and yang. Where yang is scorched, treat with water; where yin is obstructed, assist with fire. This illustrates the way in which yin and yang complement each other.

    Pulses: The strong pulse signifies heat in the chest before the guan, and upon reaching the guan, it transforms into nausea, heavy as thousands.

    Regarding the obstruction discourse: "Records of Ancient and Modern Examples" states: The five types of obstruction are due to worry, labor, food, and thought. Qi obstruction relates to palpitations and a lack of flow, leading to nausea and chest pain. Worry obstruction occurs when oppressive conditions cause reverse qi, resulting in palpitations below the heart and cold extremities. Labor obstruction leads to prolonged discomfort in the side and fullness below the ribs, causing cold extremities unable to warm themselves. Food obstruction happens when little is consumed, yet there is constant discomfort and pain in the chest, impeding breath. Thought obstruction results in palpitations, absent-mindedness, and restless eyes. All these arose from concerns, anger, and cold qi entering the chest and sides.[12p]

    　　　　　反胃

    　　寸紧尺濇，其人胸满不能食而吐，吐止者为下之，故不能食。设言未止者，此为胃反，故尺为之微濇。　　趺阳脉浮而濇，浮即为虚，濇即伤脾，脾伤即不磨，朝食暮吐，暮食朝吐，宿谷不化，名胃反。趺阳脉紧而濇，其病难治。
    　　　　济生方 【宋　严用和】

    　　　　　噎膈

    　　《素问》云：阳脉结谓之膈。盖气之与神并为阳也。逸则气神安，劳则气神耗。倘或寒温失宜，食饮乖度，七情伤感，气神俱扰，使阳气先结，阴气后乱，阴阳不和，脏腑生病，结于胸膈则成膈气，留于咽嗌则成五噎。五膈者，忧恚寒热气也；五噎者，忧思劳食气也。其为病也，令人胸膈痞闷，呕逆噎塞，妨碍饮食，胸痛彻背，或胁下支满，或心忡喜忘，咽噎气不舒。治疗之法，调顺阴阳，化痰下气，阴阳平匀，气顺痰下，膈噎之疾，无由作矣。又有下虚气上控膈，令人心下坚满痞急，肌中苦痹，缓急如刺，不得俯仰，名曰胸痹。[13p]

    Anti-Stomach Acidity

    When the stomach is tight, the person feels fullness in the chest and cannot eat, leading to vomiting. If this vomiting stops, food cannot be ingested. If one continues to experience this, it is termed "stomach reversal," hence the tightness is slightly exacerbated. The pulse at the foot yang is floating and tight; a floating pulse indicates deficiency, while tightness harms the spleen. When the spleen is harmed, digestion fails, resulting in morning vomiting of last night's food and evening vomiting of the day's meal. If food fails to digest, it is called "stomach reversal." A tight and weak pulse at the foot yang indicates a difficult-to-treat condition.

    Esophageal Obstruction

    The "Suwen" states that a knot in the yang pulse is called an obstruction. This pertains to the coalescing of qi and spirit as yang. When relaxed, qi and spirit are calm; when overworked, they deplete. If there are inappropriate temperatures or imbalanced foods, or emotional disturbances, both qi and spirit become agitated, causing the yang qi to knot, while the yin qi becomes disturbed. This results in disharmony between yin and yang, leading to organ disorders. If an obstruction occurs in the chest, it is called "obstructive qi," and if it remains in the throat, it leads to five types of choking. The five obstructions are caused by worries, anger, cold, heat, and qi disturbances; the five choke types come from worries, overthinking, labor, and eating issues. The symptoms include chest tightness, feelings of oppression, nausea, choking sensations, hindrance in eating, chest pain radiating to the back, discomfort below the ribs, a feeling of restlessness, and difficulty in swallowing. The treatment method involves regulating yin and yang, transforming phlegm, dispersing qi, achieving balance between yin and yang, which allows for smooth qi and phlegm downwards, resolving obstructions. Moreover, when there is deficiency below and qi rising, it causes a firm fullness in the heart area, discomfort in the muscles, pain like a needle, and difficulty bending or stretching, known as chest obstruction.
    [13p]

    　　　　儒门事亲 【元　张从政】

    　　　　　斥十膈五噎浪分支派疏

    　　病派之分，自巢氏始也。病失其本，亦自巢氏始也。何者？老子曰：少则得，多则惑。且俗谓噎食一证，在《内经》苦无多语，惟曰三阳结谓之膈。三阳者，谓大肠、小肠、膀胱也。结谓结热也。小肠热结则血脉燥，大肠热结则后不圊，膀胱热结则津液涸，三阳既结则前后闭塞。下既不通，必反上行，此所以噎食不下，纵下而复出也。谓胃为水谷之海，日受其新以易其陈，一日一便，乃常度也。今病噎者，三日、五日或五七日不便，是乖其度也亦明矣。[14p]

    The Confucian Way of Serving One's Parents 【Yuan Dynasty, Zhang Congzheng】

            An Analysis of the Division of the Ten and the Fifteen Classes of Disorders

    Disorders began with the nest of the Chao clan. The loss of the essence also began with this nest. Why is this? Laozi said: "Less leads to gain, more leads to confusion." Moreover, it is commonly said that choking on food is connected to the "Inner Canon" which says little more, only that the three yangs belong to the diaphragm. The three yangs refer to the large intestine, small intestine, and bladder. "Congested" means heat accumulation. If there is heat accumulation in the small intestine, the blood vessels become dry; if in the large intestine, there is inability to defecate; if in the bladder, bodily fluids dry up. When the three yangs are congested, both front and back are obstructed. When the lower passage does not open, it must reverse and move upwards, resulting in food not being able to descend properly, even if it does, it comes back up. The stomach is known as the sea of water and grains, daily receiving the new to replace the old, leading to regular bowel movements. Now those who suffer from choking are often unable to pass stool for three, five, or even five to seven days, which clearly indicates a deviation from this regularity.[14p]

    岂非三阳俱结于下，广肠枯涸，所食之物为咽所拒，纵入太仓，还出咽嗌，此阳火不下推而上行也。故经曰：少阳所至为呕涌溢，食不下。此理岂不晓然？又气厥论云：肝移寒于心为狂，膈中。阳气与寒相薄，故膈食而中不通，此膈阳与寒为之也，非独专于寒也。六节脏象又云：人迎四盛以上为格阳。王太仆云：阳盛之极，故格拒而食不得入。《正理论》曰：格则吐逆。故膈亦当为格。后世强分为五噎，谓气忧食思劳也。后又分为十膈五噎，其派既多，其惑滋甚。人之溢食，初未必遽然也。初或伤酒食，或胃热欲吐，或冒风欲吐。[15p]

    Is it not the case that the three Yang energies are all congealed below, causing the large intestine to dry up, leading to the foods consumed being rejected by the throat? Even if they enter the great warehouse, they still emerge from the throat; this is the Yang fire not being pushed down but instead rising. Therefore, the classics say: "When Shao Yang reaches, it causes vomiting and leakage, and food does not go down." Isn't this reasoning clear?

    Furthermore, the "Treatise on Qi Disorders" states: "When the liver transmits cold to the heart, it causes madness in the diaphragm. The Yang energy is weakened by cold; hence, there is impeded digestion and obstruction in the diaphragm; this is due to the interaction of Yang and cold, not solely dependent on cold." The "Six Qi and Organ Patterns" also states: "The pulse of 'Ren Ying' above four fullnesses signifies an obstruction of Yang." Wang Taipu remarked: "When Yang is at its peak, it obstructs and rejects, causing food to fail to enter." The "Zheng Li Lun" states: "Obstruction causes vomiting and regurgitation." Thus, the diaphragm must also be in a state of obstruction.

    Later generations hastily divided conditions into five types of choking, attributing them to worries over Qi, food, and labor. Later still, they divided them into ten types of obstruction and five types of choking, leading to a plethora of classifications and increasing confusion. The issue of overeating in a person does not usually manifest all at once. Initially, it may cause harm from alcohol and food, or stomach heat might induce vomiting, or dizziness from wind might lead to vomiting.[15p]

    医氏不察本源，火里烧姜，汤中煮桂；丁香未已，豆蔻继之，荜茇未已，胡椒继之。虽曰和胃，胃本不寒；虽曰补胃，胃本不虚。设如伤饮，止可逐饮，设如伤食，止可逐食。岂可言虚，便将热补？素热无者，于法犹非。素热之人，三阳必结。三阳既结，食必上潮。医氏犹云胃寒不纳，燔针钻肉，炷艾灼肌，苦楚万千。三阳热结，分明一句，到了难从，不过抽薪，最为紧要。扬汤止沸，愈急愈增。岁月弥深，为医所误。人言可下，退阳养阴，张眼吐舌，恐伤元气，止在冲和，闭塞不通，经无来路。肠宜通畅，是以肠鸣。肠既不通，遂成噎病。[16p]

    The physicians do not investigate the root cause; they burn ginger in the fire and boil cinnamon in broth. Though cloves have not yet finished, cardamom follows; though spikenard has not yet finished, pepper follows. Even if it is said to harmonize the stomach, the stomach is originally not cold; even if it is said to nourish the stomach, the stomach is originally not deficient. If it is due to harm from drinking, one can only eliminate the drink; if it is due to harm from eating, one can only eliminate the food. How can one claim deficiency and then use heating tonics? Those who originally have no excess heat are still not within the scope of treatment. Those with pre-existing heat in the body will inevitably have the three yangs converge. Once the three yangs converge, food will inevitably rise. The physician still claims the stomach is cold and cannot accept; burning needles into flesh, moxibustion scorching the skin, enduring countless agonies. The heat of the three yangs converging is clear, but treatment is difficult; merely withdrawing stimuli is of utmost importance. It is like trying to stop boiling water with more heat—painful and counterproductive. Over time, this has led to mistakes by physicians. People say to descend the yang and nourish the yin, opening the eyes and sticking out the tongue, fearing harm to the original energy, but all is merely about maintaining harmony, obstructed and unresponsive, without any way forward. The intestines should be unobstructed, hence the noises they make. When the intestines are obstructed, it leads to choking illness.[16p]

    世传五噎宽中散，有姜有桂；十膈散，有附有乌。今予既斥其方，信乎与否，以听后贤。或云忧恚气结，亦可下乎？余曰：忧恚(石盘)礡，便同大郁。太仓公见下法既废，千年不复。今代刘河间治膈气噎食用三承气汤，独超近代。今予姑示后人，用药之时，更详轻重。假如闭久，慎勿陡攻。纵得攻开，必虑后患。宜先润养，小着汤丸，累累加之，关扃自透。其或咽噎，上阻涎痰，轻用苦酸，微微涌出，因而治下，药势易行。设或不行，蜜盐下导，始终勾引，两药相通，结散阳消，饮食自下。莫将巴豆，耗却天真，液燥津枯，留毒不去。人言此病，宜下夺之。从下夺来，转虚转痞。[17p]

    Traditionally, there are five types of constriction in the diaphragm, with ingredients like ginger and cinnamon; and ten types of obstruction with additions of certain substances. Now, I have dismissed those methods, believing them to be questionable, allowing future scholars to judge. Some say that worry and anger can cause stagnation; can they be treated? I say: worry and anger cause blockages, identical to significant distress. Master Tai Cang noted that once established, these methods become obsolete and won't return for a thousand years.

    In our time, Liu Hejian's treatment for obstructed qi and food, using the Three承气 Decoction, stands out uniquely in modernity. I now suggest to future generations that when using medicine, they should carefully consider the dosage. If the obstruction has persisted for a long time, do not attack aggressively. Even if one manages to resolve the obstruction, one must be cautious of future issues. It is best to first moisten and nourish the body with smaller doses of medicinal pills, gradually increasing them until the blockage naturally eases.

    If there is choking or obstruction, resulting in phlegm, one can lightly use bitter and sour herbs to gently induce flow, and then treat accordingly; the medicine will be more effective. If that does not work, one can guide with honey and salt, ensuring a continuous interaction between the two medicines, promoting dispersion and consumption of stagnation. Do not use ba dou, as it exhausts the body's natural essence, drying up fluids and leaving toxins within. Some say this condition should be treated by expelling it; however, expelling it can lead to emptiness and discomfort.[17p]

    　　　　东垣十书 【元　李杲】

    　　　　　噎塞治法

    　　堵塞咽喉，阳气不得出者曰塞，阴气不得下降者曰噎。夫噎塞迎逆于咽喉胸膈之间，令诸经不行，则口开目瞪，气欲绝。当先用辛甘气味俱阳之药，引胃气以治其本，加堵塞之药以泻其标也。寒月阴气大助阴邪于外，于正药内加吴茱萸大热大辛苦之味，以泻阴寒之气。暑月阳盛，则于正药中加青皮、陈皮、益智、黄蘗散寒气，泄阴火之上逆，或以消痞丸合滋肾丸。滋肾丸者，黄蘗、知母，微加肉桂三味是也。或更加黄连别作丸，二药七八十丸，空心约宿食消尽服之，待少时以美食压之，不令胃中停留也。[18p]

    Eastern Garden Ten Treatises
    By Li Gao, Yuan Dynasty

    Treatment of Choking and Blockage

    When the throat is blocked, preventing yang qi from emerging, it is called blockage; when yin qi cannot descend, it is called choking. Blockage and choking oppose the flow between the throat and chest, causing stagnation in the channels; then the mouth may open and the eyes may bulge, leading to a near suffocation feeling. First, one should use medicinal herbs with spicy and sweet flavors that are entirely yang to stimulate the stomach qi and address the root cause, supplemented by herbs to relieve the blockage. During the cold months, when the yin energy greatly strengthens external yin pathogens, one should add Wu Zhu Yu, which has a strongly hot and spicy flavor, to the primary medicine to dispel the cold yin qi. In the hot months, when yang is strong, add Qing Pi, Chen Pi, Yi Zhi, and Huang Lian to scatter the cold qi and release the upward counterflow of yin fire, or combine with Xiao Pi Wan and Zi Shen Wan. The Zi Shen Wan consists of Huang Lian, Zhi Mu, and slightly added Rou Gui, totaling three ingredients. Alternatively, one might add Huang Lian to create a special pill, producing seventy or eighty pills, to be taken on an empty stomach until the food from the previous meal is completely digested, followed by light and delicious foods to prevent stagnation in the stomach.[18p]

    　　　　　膈咽不通四时换气用药法

    　　《针经》曰：胃病者，腹(月真)胀，胃脘当心而痛，上支两胁，膈咽不通，饮食不下，取三里。夫咽者咽物之门户，膈者心肺之分野。不通者，升降之气不得上下交通。又云清气在下，则生飧泄，谓泄黄如糜，米谷不化也。浊气在上，则生(月真)胀，不得大便或大便难，先结后溏皆是也。浊气在上，当降而不降者，乃肾肝吸入之阴气，不得下而反在上，胃气逆上，或为呕为吐为哕者，是阴火上冲而吸入之气不得入，故食不得下。此皆气冲之火，逆胃之脉反上而作者也。[19p]

    Methods for Using Medicinal Herbs to Treat Impediments in the Throat and Diaphragm Causing Discomfort

    The "Acupuncture Classic" states: For stomach illnesses, there is abdominal distension, pain in the epigastric region, discomfort in both sides of the chest, impediment in the throat and diaphragm, and inability to consume food or drink. The point to be selected is Sanli. The throat is the gateway for swallowing food, while the diaphragm separates the heart and lungs. When there is an obstruction, the ascending and descending vital energies cannot communicate freely. It is also said that if clear energy is in the lower region, it leads to food retention, resulting in diarrhea that is yellow and like paste, indicating that grains are not being digested. Conversely, if turbid energy rises, it causes abdominal distension, leading to difficulties in defecation; either constipation or diarrhea may ensue. When the turbid energy is stuck above and should descend but does not, the yin energy drawn in by the kidneys and liver cannot move downwards and instead remains trapped, causing the stomach's energy to rebel upwards, resulting in nausea, vomiting, or belching. This is due to the upward surge of yin fire conflicting with the incoming energy, preventing food from being ingested. All of this is caused by the fire of obstructed energy, reversing the flow of the stomach's channels upwards.[19p]

    清气在下，则生飧泄者，胃气未病之日，当上行心肺而荣经，因饮食失节，劳役形体，心火乘于土位，胃气弱而下陷入阴中，故米谷入而不得升降，为飧泄也。咽膈之间，壅遏之甚，不得交通者，皆冲脉上行，逆气所作也。盖胃病者，上冲两胁，膈咽不通，　饮食不下，当取之三里。《针经》云：清浊相干，乱于胸中，是为大悗。大悗者，惑也。气不交通，最为急证，不急去之，诸变生矣。治法：阳气不足，阴气有余，先补其阳，后泻其阴，是先令阳气升发于阳分而后泻阴也。春夏之月，阳气在经，当益其经脉，去其血络；秋冬阳气降伏，当先治其脏腑。[20p]

    When the clear energy descends, it leads to symptoms of food retention. On days when the stomach energy is not ill, it should rise to support the heart and lungs and nourish the channels. However, due to irregularities in diet and excessive labor on the body, the heart fire occupies the earth’s position, weakening the stomach energy and causing it to sink into the yin. Thus, when grains enter but cannot ascend or descend, it results in food retention. The space between the throat and diaphragm is severely obstructed, preventing communication, all of which is caused by the counterflow of the penetrating vessel. Stomach ailments cause upward disruption in both flanks, and with the throat and diaphragm not open, food cannot descend, so one must choose points on the stomach meridian (Zu San Li). The "Classic of Acupuncture" states that when clear and turbid energies are mixed and disordered in the chest, it is called great disturbance. Great disturbance refers to confusion. When energy does not circulate properly, it is a critical condition. If not urgently addressed, various changes will occur.

    Treatment principle: When there is insufficient yang energy and excess yin energy, one should first tonify the yang and then drain the yin; this ensures that yang energy rises in the yang aspect before draining yin. In the spring and summer months, when yang energy is present in the channels, one should enhance the meridians and eliminate blood stasis; in autumn and winter when yang energy is subdued, one must first treat the internal organs.[20p]

    塞者五脏之所主，阴也，血也；噎者，六腑之所主，阳也，气也。二者皆由阴中伏阳而作也。今立四时用药法，并治法于后。　　冬三月，阴气在外，阳气在内，当外助阳气，不得发汗，内消阴火，勿令泄泻，此闭密之大要也。盛冬乃水旺之时，水旺则金旺，子能令母实，肺者肾之母，皮毛之阳，元本虚弱，更以冬月助其令，故病者善嚏，鼻流清涕，寒甚则浊涕嚏不止，比常人尤大恶风寒，小便数而欠，或上咳下便，色清而多，大便不调，常夜无寐，甚则为痰嗽呕哕，吐唾白沫，以至口开目瞪，气不交通欲绝者，吴茱萸丸主之。[21p]

    The spleen governs the five organs, associated with yin and blood; the esophagus governs the six bowels, associated with yang and qi. Both arise from the latent yang within the yin. Now, I will establish methods for administering medicine and treatments corresponding to the four seasons.

    In winter, during the three months, yin energy is external, and yang energy is internal. One should support the yang from outside without inducing sweating, eliminating internal yin fire and preventing leakage; this is essential for confinement. Deep winter is when water is at its peak, and when water is abundant, metal becomes strong. The child (organs) can make the mother (organs) substantial. The lungs are the mother of the kidneys, and the skin and hair represent yang. If the original condition is weak, reinforcing it with winter will exacerbate the symptoms. Therefore, patients often sneeze, have a runny nose with clear mucus, and in severe cold, they may produce thick mucus and sneeze incessantly. They are particularly intolerant of wind and cold, have frequent and scanty urination, and may cough up large amounts of clear phlegm, with disordered bowel movements, sleepless nights, and in severe cases, may manifest as phlegm cough, vomiting white froth, leading to wide-open mouth and bulging eyes, with breathing difficulties nearing cessation. For such symptoms, the prescription of Wu Zhu Yu Pills is indicated.[21p]

    　　夏三月大暑，阳气在外，阴气在内，以此病值此时，是天助正气而銼其邪气，不治而自愈矣。然亦有当愈不愈者，盖阴气极盛正气不能伸故耳。且如膈咽不通，咽中梗盛者，前证俱作，治法当从时用利膈丸泻肺火，以黄芪补中汤送下。如两足痿厥，行步恇怯，敧侧欲倒，臂臑如折，及作痛而无力，或气短促而喘，或不足以息，以黄芪、人参、甘草、白朮、苍朮、泽泻、猪苓、茯苓、陈皮等作汤，送下滋肾丸五六十丸。六七月之间，湿热之令大行，气短不能言者，加五味子、麦门冬；如心下痞闷，食不下，以上件白朮苍朮等汤，送下消痞丸七十丸，更审而用之。
    　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　关格

    　　凡关格必用吐，提其气之横格，不必在出痰也。　　有痰宜吐者，二陈汤吐之，吐中便有降。　　有中气虚不运者，补气药中升降。
    　　寒在上，热在下，脉两手寸俱盛四倍以上。[22p]

    In the third month of summer, during the great heat, the yang energy is external, while the yin energy is internal. Illness that arises at this time is supported by the heavens to strengthen the righteous qi and weaken the evil qi, allowing for self-healing without treatment. However, there are also cases where conditions that should improve do not, due to the excessive dominance of yin energy which obstructs the spread of righteous qi.

    For instance, if there is obstruction in the diaphragm and throat with severe congestion, treatment should focus on using "Li Ge Wan" to clear lung fire and then follow with "Huang Qi Bu Zhong Tang" for nourishment. If there are symptoms like weakness or numbness in the legs, stumbling when walking, a tendency to lean or fall, pain and lack of strength in the arms, or shortness of breath, one should prepare a soup with Huang Qi, Ren Shen, Gan Cao, Bai Zhu, Cang Zhu, Ze Xie, Zhu Ling, Fu Ling, and Chen Pi, and take five to sixty pills of a kidney-nourishing formula.

    Between June and July, when damp heat prevails, if there are symptoms of shortness of breath making it hard to speak, add Wu Wei Zi and Mai Men Dong. In cases of obstinate fullness and discomfort in the chest, with inability to eat, use the aforementioned soup of Bai Zhu and Cang Zhu, and take seventy pills of a formula to resolve fullness, adjusting as necessary.

    Duan Xi Xin Fa [from the Yuan dynasty, by Zhu Zhenheng]

    Regarding the treatment of obstructions, one must always use vomiting to release the obstructed qi, which does not necessarily have to involve phlegm. When phlegm is present, "Er Chen Tang" can be used to induce vomiting, which will help to descend the qi. If there is deficiency of middle qi that is not circulating properly, use tonifying herbs that aid in ascending and descending.

    If cold is present above and heat below, the pulse in both wrists will be stronger than four times the normal level.[22p]

    　　　　　翻胃

    　　翻胃大约有四：血虚、气虚、有热、有痰。兼病，必用韭汁、童便、竹沥、牛羊乳、生姜汁；气虚入四君子汤，必右手脉无力；血虚入四物汤加童便，必左手脉无力。切不可用香燥之药，若服之必死。宜薄滋味。　　治反胃，用黄连三钱，生姜汁浸炒，山楂肉二钱，保和丸二钱，同为末，糊丸如麻子大，脏脂为衣，人参汤入竹沥再煎一沸，下六十丸。　　有痰，二陈汤为主，必寸关脉沉，或伏而大。有气结，宜开滞导气之药，必寸关脉沉而濇。有内虚阴火上炎而反胃者，作阴火治之。　　年少者，四物汤清胃脘。血燥不润便故濇。年老虽不治，亦用参朮，关防气虚胃虚。气虚者，四君子汤加芦根、童便，或参苓白朮散，或韭汁、牛羊乳，或入叫驴尿。又有积血停于内而致，当消息逐之。大便濇者难治。常令食兔肉则便利。　　翻胃即膈噎，盖膈噎乃翻胃之渐，《发挥》备言年高者不治。粪如羊屎者，断不可治，大肠无血故也。[23p]

    Vomiting

    Vomiting can generally be attributed to four causes: blood deficiency, qi deficiency, heat, and phlegm. In cases with combined ailments, one must use leeks juice, children's urine, bamboo juice, cow or sheep milk, and ginger juice; for qi deficiency, it is necessary to use the Four Gentlemen Decoction, and the right wrist pulse will be weak; for blood deficiency, add children's urine to the Four Substances Decoction, and the left wrist pulse will be weak. Do not use aromatic and dry medicines, as their use would be fatal. It is advisable to favor light tastes.

    To treat vomiting, use three qian of coptis, ginger juice soaked and stir-fried, two qian of hawthorn flesh, and two qian of Baohe pills, grind into a powder, and form into pills the size of sesame seeds, coated with animal fat, then boil it in ginseng soup mixed with bamboo juice for a second boiling, yielding sixty pills.

    If there is phlegm, the Erchen Decoction should be the main treatment; the pulse at the inch position will be deep or large. If there is qi stagnation, it is advisable to use medicine that opens up and guides qi; the pulse at the inch position will be deep and thin. For internal deficiency with yin fire rising and causing vomiting, treat the yin fire.

    For the young, the Four Substances Decoction clears the stomach. Blood dryness leads to constipation. Although the elderly might not need treatment, they should use ginseng and atractylodes to prevent qi deficiency and stomach weakness. In cases of qi deficiency, use the Four Gentlemen Decoction with reed root and children's urine, or ginseng and poria powder, or leeks juice mixed with cow or sheep milk, or even donkey urine. Accumulated blood stagnating within must be resolved. If the stool is hard, treatment is difficult. Encourage eating rabbit meat for easier bowel movements.

    Vomiting is akin to esophageal blockage; indeed, esophageal blockage is a progression of vomiting. The "Elucidation" mentions that the elderly should not be treated. If the stool resembles sheep droppings, it should definitely not be treated, as the large intestine contains no blood.[23p]

    　　　　局方发挥 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　治法辨惑

    　　《局方》治气一门，有曰治一切气，冷气，滞气，逆气，上气，用安息香丸、丁沉丸、大沉香丸、苏子丸、匀气散、如神丸、集香丸、白沉香丸、煨姜丸、盐煎散、七气散、温白丸、生姜汤。其治呕吐膈噎也，用五膈丸、五膈宽中散、膈气散、酒症丸、草豆蔻丸、撞气丸、人参丁香散。其治吞酸也，用丁香煎丸、小理中丸。其治痰饮也，用倍朮丸、消饮丸、温中化痰丸、五套丸。且于各方条下，或曰口苦失味，曰噫酸，曰舌濇，曰吐清水，曰痞满，曰气急，曰胁下急痛，曰五心中热，口烂生疮，皆是明言热证，何为悉用热药？夫周流于人之一身以为主者气也，阳往则阴来，阴往则阳来，一升一降，无有穷已。[24p]

    The "Jufang" focuses on the treatment of qi disorders. It discusses treating various types of qi such as cold qi, stagnant qi, counterflow qi, and upper qi using remedies like Anxi Xiang Pill, Ding Chen Pill, Da Chen Xiang Pill, Suzi Pill, Yungqi Powder, Renshen Pill, Jixiang Pill, Bai Chen Xiang Pill, Wei Jiang Pill, Yan Jian Powder, Qi Qi Powder, Wen Bai Pill, and Sheng Jiang Decoction.

    For treating vomiting and esophageal obstruction, it recommends Wu Ge Pill, Wu Ge Kuanzhong Powder, Ge Qi Powder, Jiu Zheng Pill, Cao Dou Kou Pill, Zhuan Qi Pill, and Renshen Dingxiang Powder. For sour belching, it advises using Dingxiang Decoction Pill and Xiao Lizhong Pill. To address phlegm and fluid retention, it suggests Bei Zhu Pill, Xiaoyin Pill, Wen Zhong Hua Tan Pill, and Wu Tao Pill.

    Additionally, in each section, it mentions symptoms such as bitter mouth, loss of taste, sour belching, clear water vomiting, fullness and pressure, breathlessness, urgent pain in the side, heat in the five hearts, and mouth ulcers, all of which clearly indicate heat syndrome. Therefore, why use heat medicine for all? The life force circulating within a person is primarily qi; when yang rises, yin descends, and vice versa, with movements always in balance, without end.[24p]

    苟内不伤于七情，外不感于六淫，其为气也，何病之有！今曰冷气、滞气、逆气、上气，皆是肺受火邪，气得炎上之化，有升无降，熏蒸清道，甚而至于上焦不纳，中焦不化，下焦不渗，展转变为呕吐，膈噎，痰饮，反胃，吞酸。夫治寒以热，治热以寒，此正治之法也；治热用热，治寒用寒，此反佐之法也。详味前方，既非正治，又非反佐，此愚之所以不能无疑也。谨按《原病式》曰：诸病呕吐酸，皆属于热。诸积饮痞满中膈，皆属于湿。[25p]

    If one is not hurt internally by the Seven Emotions, nor influenced externally by the Six Excesses, what illness could there be! Now, what is called cold qi, stagnant qi, rebellious qi, and rising qi, all stem from the lung being invaded by fire pathogens, causing the qi to transform upwards, with ascent but no descent, suffocating and steaming the clear pathways, to the extent that the upper burner fails to receive, the middle burner fails to transform, and the lower burner fails to penetrate, leading to changes such as vomiting, esophageal obstruction, phlegm and fluid accumulation, retrograde swallowing, and sour regurgitation. To treat cold, use heat; to treat heat, use cold—this is the correct method of treatment. Using heat to treat heat, or using cold to treat cold, is contrary to the principles of support. Reflecting on the earlier sections, neither pertains to the correct treatment nor to the method of support, which is why I cannot avoid doubts. According to the "Original Disease Form," it states: all illnesses of vomiting sourness relate to heat. All accumulations of fluids and fullness in the middle burner relate to dampness.[25p]

    诸气逆冲，上呕涌溢，食不下，皆属于火。诸坚痞腹满急痛，吐腥秽，皆属于寒。深契仲景之意。《金匮要略》曰：胸痹病，胸背痛，栝蒌薤白汤主之。胸痹，心痛彻背，背痛彻心，栝蒌薤白半夏汤主之。心下痞气，气结在胸胁下，上逆抢心者，枳实薤白栝蒌桂枝汤主之。呕而心下痞者，半夏泻心汤主之。干呕而利者，黄芩加半夏生姜汤主之。诸呕吐谷不得入者，小半夏汤主之。呕吐病在膈上者，猪苓汤主之。胃反呕吐者，半夏参蜜汤主之。食已即吐者，大黄甘草汤主之。胃反吐而渴者，茯苓泽泻汤主之。[26p]

    Various qi rebel, causing upward vomiting and overflow, inability to eat, all belong to fire. Various hard accumulations, fullness of the abdomen, urgent pain, and foul vomiting, all belong to cold. This deeply aligns with the meaning of Zhongjing. The "Synopsis of the Golden Chamber" states: for chest obstruction disease with pain in the chest and back, Guo Lou and Xi Bai Decoction is the principal remedy. Chest obstruction with heart pain penetrating to the back, and back pain penetrating to the heart, Guo Lou, Xi Bai, and Ban Xia Decoction is the principal remedy. For qi stagnation under the heart, with qi blocked in the chest and under the ribs, rebellious heart qi, Zhi Shi, Xi Bai, Guo Lou, and Gui Zhi Decoction is the principal remedy. For vomiting and qi stagnation under the heart, Ban Xia Xie Xin Decoction is the principal remedy. For dry vomiting with diarrhea, Huang Qin plus Ban Xia and Sheng Jiang Decoction is the principal remedy. For vomiting grains unable to enter, Xiao Ban Xia Decoction is the principal remedy. For vomiting due to issues in the diaphragm, Zhu Ling Decoction is the principal remedy. For gastric reflux causing vomiting, Ban Xia, Ren Shen, and Honey Decoction is the principal remedy. For vomiting immediately after eating, Da Huang and Gan Cao Decoction is the principal remedy. For gastric reflux with thirst, Fu Ling and Ze Xie Decoction is the principal remedy.[26p]

    吐后欲饮者，文蛤汤主之。病似呕不呕，似哕不哕，心中无奈者，姜汁半夏汤主之。干呕手足冷者，陈皮汤主之。哕逆者，陈皮竹茹汤主之。干呕下利者，黄芩汤主之。气冲上者，皂荚丸主之。上气脉浮者，厚朴麻黄汤主之。上气脉沉者，泽泻汤主之。火逆上气者，麦门冬汤主之。心下有痰饮，胸胁支满，目眩，茯苓桂朮汤主之。短气有微饮，当从小便出，宜茯苓桂朮甘草汤主之，肾气丸亦主之。病者脉伏，其人欲自利，利者反快，虽利心下续坚满者，此为留饮欲去故也，甘遂半夏汤主之。病悬饮者，十枣汤主之。病溢饮者，当发其汗，宜大青龙汤，又宜小青龙汤主之。心下有支饮，其人苦冒眩，泽泻汤主之。支饮胸满者，厚朴大黄汤主之。支饮不得息，葶苈大枣泻肺汤主之。呕家本渴，今反不渴，心中有支饮故也，小半夏汤主之。[27p]

    For those who want to drink after vomiting, use clam soup. For a patient feeling like they might vomit but not actually doing so, or feeling a sense of helplessness, ginger and pinellia soup is indicated. For dry heaving with cold hands and feet, use tangerine peel soup. For reverse belching, tangerine peel and bamboo shavings soup is suitable. For dry heaving accompanied by diarrhea, use scutellaria soup. For those with rising qi, use soap pod pills. For rising qi with a floating pulse, use magnolia bark and ephedra soup. For rising qi with a sinking pulse, use alisma soup. For heat reversing upward qi, use ophiopogon soup. If there is phlegm and fluid in the heart area, fullness in the chest and sides, and dizziness, use poria, cinnamon, and astragalus soup. For shortness of breath with minor fluid accumulation, which should be regulated through urination, poria, cinnamon, astragalus, and licorice soup is suitable, and kidney qi pills are also effective. If the patient's pulse is deep and they want to relieve themselves but feel discomfort from retained fluid, use sweet saline and pinellia soup. If the patient has retained fluid, use ten jujube soup. For overflowing fluid, sweat must be induced; daqinglong soup and xiaoqinglong soup are appropriate. For fluid retention in the heart area causing significant dizziness, alisma soup is indicated. For chest fullness with fluid retention, use magnolia bark and rhubarb soup. If unable to breathe due to fluid retention, use artemisia and jujube soup for lung drainage. If previously thirsty due to vomiting, but now not thirsty because of fluid retention, use small pinellia soup.[27p]

    卒呕吐心下痞，膈间有水，眩悸者，小半夏加茯苓汤主之。假令瘦人脐下有悸者，吐涎沫而头眩，此水也，五苓散主之。心胸有停痰宿水，自吐出水后，心胸间虚气满不能食，消痰气令能食，茯苓饮主之。先渴后呕，为水停心下，此属饮家，半夏汤加茯苓主之。观其微意，可表者汗之，可下者利之，滞者导之，郁者扬之，热者清之，寒者温之，偏寒偏热者反佐而行之，挟湿者淡以渗之，挟虚者补而养之。何尝例用辛香燥热之剂，以火济火，实实虚虚，咎将谁执？或曰：《脉诀》谓热则生风，冷生气，寒主收引。今冷气上冲矣，气逆气滞矣，非冷而何？吾子引仲景之言而斥其非，然则诸气痰饮、呕吐、反胃、吞酸等病，将无寒证耶？予曰：五脏各有火，五志激之，其火随起。若诸寒为病，必须身犯寒气，口食寒物，乃为病寒，非若诸火病自内作，所以气之病寒者，十无一二。或曰：其余痰气呕吐、吞酸、噎膈、反胃，作热作火论治，于理可通。[28p]

    When there is vomiting, a feeling of fullness in the heart, and water between the diaphragm, along with dizziness and palpitations, the prescription is Xiao Banxia Jia Fuling Decoction. If a thin person has palpitations below the navel, nausea with frothy saliva, and dizziness, this signifies water, and the prescription is Wuling Powder. If there is stagnant phlegm and retained water in the chest, after expelling the water, if there remains a sensation of fullness and inability to eat, we must resolve the phlegm and air to restore appetite; Fuling Drink is indicated. If there is thirst followed by vomiting, indicating water retention in the heart area, this is classified under drink-related ailments, and the prescription is Banxia Decoction with Fuling.

    In observing subtle signs, if there is excessive sweating that can be expressed, it should be encouraged; if there is stagnation, it should be guided out; if there is depression, it should be uplifted; if there is heat, it should be cleared; if there is cold, it should be warmed; if there is a mix of cold and heat, we should counterbalance and proceed accordingly; if dampness is involved, it should be diluted and drained; if deficiency is present, it should be nourished and supplemented. One must not routinely use pungent and warming agents to address fire with fire—who will be blamed for this?

    Some say: "The Pulse Classic states that heat causes wind, coolness generates qi, and cold promotes contraction.” Now, if cool air rises and qi is in rebellion and stagnation, how can it be anything but coolness? You quote Zhang Zhongjing's words to refute me, yet do all ailments of qi, phlegm, drink, vomiting, and acid reflux lack cold symptoms? I say: The five organs each possess their fire, ignited by the five emotions; this fire rises accordingly. If all ailments arise from cold, one must be exposed to cold air or consume cold food for it to truly be a cold illness—not merely internal fire diseases, of which there are rarely one or two cases of cold affecting qi.

    Some argue that other symptoms like phlegm, qi, vomiting, acid reflux, and choking sensation are treated on the basis of heat and fire, which is reasonable enough.[28p]

    若病人自言冷气从下而上，非冷而何？予曰：上升之气自肝而出，中挟相火自下而出，其热为甚，自觉其冷，非真冷也，火极似水，积热之甚，阳亢阴微，故见此证冷生气者，出高阳生之谬言也。若病果因于寒，当以去寒之剂治之，何至例用辛香燥热为方？不知权变，宁不误人？或曰：气上升者，皆用黑锡丹、养正丹、养气丹等药，以为镇坠，然服之者随手得效，吾子以为热甚之病，亦将有悞耶？予曰：相火之外，又有脏腑厥阳之火。五志之动，各有火起。相火者，经所谓一水不胜二火之火。斯火也，出于天造。厥阳者，经所谓一水不胜五火之火，出于人欲。[29p]

    If a patient claims that cold energy rises from below, what can it be but cold? I said: The ascending energy emerges from the liver, while the intermingled fire arises from below, producing intense heat, which the patient perceives as cold; it is not true cold. When the fire is at its peak, it resembles water — the accumulation of excessive heat leads to an overabundance of Yang and a deficiency of Yin, hence this symptom of cold arising from energy is a misconception stemming from misguided theories.

    If the illness truly arises from cold, it should be treated with remedies to dispel cold. Why resort to conventional methods using pungent, aromatic, and warming prescriptions? Ignoring the need for adaptability leads to potentially misleading treatments. Some say that for rising energy, one should use medicines like Heixi Dan, Yangzheng Dan, and Yangqi Dan to stabilize it. Those who take these medicines may find quick relief, but do you think that a disease marked by intense heat won't yield errors?

    I replied: In addition to the associated fire, there is also the Yang fire within the organs. The movements of emotions each give rise to their own fires. The associated fire, as referred to in the scriptures, is the fire of "one water cannot withstand two fires." This fire originates from heavenly creation. The Yang fire, according to the texts, is the fire of "one water cannot withstand five fires," arising from human desires.[29p]

    二者之火相扇而动，气之升也，随火炎上，升而不降，孰能御之？今借丹剂之重坠而降之，气郁为湿痰，丹性热燥，湿痰被劫，亦为暂开，所以清快。丹毒积久，偏助狂火，阴血愈耗，其升愈甚。俗人喜温，迷而不悟，被此祸者，滔滔皆是。或曰：丹药之重，欲降而升，然如之何则可？予曰：投以辛凉，行以辛温，制伏肝邪；治以咸寒，佐以甘温，收以苦甘，和以甘淡，补养阴血。阳自相附，阴阳比和，何升之有？先哲治法，其则不远，吾不赘及。或曰：诸气诸饮，与夫呕吐吞酸、膈噎反胃等证，《局方》未中肯綮，我知之矣。然则《要略》之方，果足用乎？抑犹有未发者乎？予曰：天地之气化无穷，人身之病亦变化无穷。仲景之书，载道者也。医之良者，引例推类，可谓无穷之用，借令略有加减修合，终难逾越矩度。[30p]

    The fire from both sides stirs and moves, its energy rising along with the flame, ascending without descending—who can resist it? Now, by employing heavy dan pills to bring it down, the energy becomes stagnant and transforms into damp phlegm. The nature of the dan is hot and dry; damp phlegm is thus affected and temporarily resolved, resulting in relief. When dan toxicity accumulates over time, it further fuels the fiery excess, depleting yin blood and causing even more ascendance. Common people favor warmth, remaining oblivious and falling victim to this disaster—many are affected. Some say: the heaviness of dan pills seeks to descend yet does ascend; how then can this be resolved? I say: administer pungent coolness to dispel and use pungent warmth to subdue liver evils; treat with salty coldness, supplemented by sweet warmth, collecting bitterness and sweetness, harmonizing with mild sweetness to nourish yin blood. When yang is self-sustaining and yin and yang are harmonized, what is there left to ascend? The methods of ancient sages are not far removed; I will not elaborate further. Some say: various airs and drinks, along with symptoms like nausea, sour regurgitation, and stomach distress—are not adequately addressed in the “Jufang” text; I understand this. However, is the formula in the “Yao Lue” truly sufficient? Or are there still unidentified issues? I say: the transformations of the energies of heaven and earth are endless, and the diseases of the human body are equally variable. The book of Zhongjing carries the essence of the teachings. Good physicians draw on examples and analogies, which can be said to be of infinite utility, even if slight adjustments are made, they will ultimately not exceed the established standards.[30p]

    夫气之初病也，其端甚微，或因些小饮食不谨，或外冒风雨寒暑，或内感七情，或食味过厚，偏助阳气，积成膈热；或资禀素实，表密无汗，或性急易怒，阴火炎上，以致津液不行，清浊相干，气为之病；或痞痛不思食，或噎噫腐气吞酸，或嘈杂膨满，不求本原，便认为寒，遽以辛香燥热之剂投之，数贴暂得快然，以为神方，仍前厚味不节，将理不谨，旧疾被劫，暂舒浊液，易于攒聚，或半月一月，前病复作，如此延蔓，自气成积，自积成痰，此为痰饮吞酸之由也。[31p]

    At the onset, illness manifests as simple disturbances. Its origins are often quite subtle, stemming from minor dietary indiscretions, exposure to wind and rain, fluctuations in temperature, emotional disturbances, excessive richness of food that bolsters yang energy, leading to the accumulation of heat in the diaphragm; or a robust constitution with a closed surface and no sweating, or a temperament that is easily angered, causing yin fire to rise and obstruct the flow of fluids, mixing the clear and turbid, resulting in illness; or experiencing distension and pain without appetite, or symptoms like hiccups and sour regurgitation, or a sense of fullness and bloating, without seeking the root cause, one mistakenly concludes it is due to cold and hastily treats it with pungent and warming substances, temporarily finding relief and mistaking it for a miraculous remedy, while continuing to indulge in rich flavors without restraint. This leads to carelessness, exacerbating past ailments, momentarily relieving the turbid fluids, which are then easily re-accumulated. The cycle may repeat in half a month or a month, with the previous illness returning. Thus, this prolongation leads to the accumulation of qi and the formation of phlegm, which causes sour regurgitation.[31p]

    良工未遇，谬药已行，痰挟瘀血，遂成窠囊，于是为痞痛呕吐、噎膈反胃之次第，诸证蜂起，饮食汤液，泥滞不行，渗道蹇濇，大便或秘或溏，下失传化，中焦愈停。医者不察，犹执为冷，翻思前药，随手得快，至此宾主皆恨药欠燥热，颙俟久服，脾可以温，胃可以壮，以冀一旦豁然之效。不思胃为水谷之海，多血多气，气清和则能受；脾为消化之官，气清和则能运。今得香热之药，偏助气血沸腾。其始也，胃液凝聚，无所容受；其久也，脾气耗散，传化渐迟。其有胃热易饥，急于得食，脾伤不磨，郁积成痛，医者犹曰虚而积寒，非寻常草木可疗，妄以乌附助佐丹剂，专意服饵。积而久也，血液俱耗，胃脘干槁。[32p]

    A skilled physician has not been found, yet misguided treatments have been promulgated. Phlegm mixed with stagnant blood has formed a mass, leading to symptoms such as fullness, pain, vomiting, and difficulty swallowing, along with a range of issues arising from these conditions. The intake of food and fluids has become stagnated, with pathways congested and bowel movements either obstructed or loose, resulting in a disruption of transformation and transportation in the middle burner. Physicians, not perceiving this, continue to attribute it to cold, thinking back to previous remedies and hastily seeking immediate relief. Consequently, both doctor and patient lament that the medicinal treatments lack the necessary warmth and dryness, hoping that with prolonged use, the spleen might be warmed and the stomach strengthened, anticipating that one day, results will be achieved. They fail to realize that the stomach is the sea of food and fluids, rich in blood and Qi; when the Qi is clear and harmonious, it can receive; the spleen is the organ of digestion, and when the Qi is clear and harmonious, it can function properly. However, the use of fragrant and warming medicines merely exacerbates the boiling of Qi and blood. Initially, the gastric juices become congealed and unable to receive. Over time, the spleen's Qi is depleted, leading to delayed transformations. With heat in the stomach causing easy hunger and urgency for food, the spleen is damaged and unexercised, resulting in accumulated pain. Physicians still claim it to be vacuity accompanied by cold. This is not something that ordinary herbs and plants can treat; instead, they recklessly use substances to assist and complement the dry pills, focusing solely on consuming them. As time passes, both blood and fluids are depleted, leaving the stomach and intestines dry and desiccated.[32p]

    其槁在上，近咽之下，水饮可行，食物难入，间或可入，入亦不多，名之曰噎；其槁在下，与胃为近，食虽可入，难尽入胃，良久复出，名之曰膈，亦曰反胃。大便秘小，若羊屎然，名虽不同，病出一体。《要略》论饮有六，曰痰饮、悬饮、溢饮、支饮、留饮、伏饮，分别五脏诸证治法，至矣尽矣。但恨医者不善处治，病者不守禁忌，遂使药助病邪，展转病痼，去生渐远，深可哀悯。或曰：《千金》诸方，治膈噎反胃，未尝废姜桂等剂，何吾子之多言也？予曰：气之郁滞，久留清道，非借香热不足以行。[33p]

    When the obstruction is above, near the throat, liquids can pass, but solid food is difficult to swallow; occasionally, it may go down, but not much, this is called "choking." When the obstruction is below, near the stomach, food can enter, but it's hard to completely fill the stomach; after a while, it comes back up, this is called "retention" or "reflux." If the stool is constipated and small, resembling sheep droppings, although the names differ, the illness originates from the same cause.

    In the "Yao Lue," there are six types of drinking issues: phlegm retention, suspended fluid, overflow fluid, obstructive fluid, retained fluid, and hidden fluid, each with different treatment methods related to the five organs, which are comprehensive and thorough. However, it is lamentable that practitioners do not manage treatments well, and patients do not adhere to restrictions, which leads to medication exacerbating the illness, causing a cycle of chronic conditions, drifting further from health—a situation truly worthy of sympathy.

    Some say: "In the 'Qian Jin' recipes for treating retention, choking, and reflux, ginger and cinnamon have never been omitted; why then does my disciple speak so much?" I respond: The stagnation and retention of qi, if left in the clear pathways for too long, cannot be resolved without the assistance of warming and aromatic herbs.[33p]

    然悉有大黄、石膏、竹茹、芒硝、泽泻、前胡、(石卜)硝、茯苓、黄芩、芦根、(艹舌)蒌等药，为之佐使，其始则同，其终则异，病邪易伏，故易于安。或曰：胃脘干槁者，古方果可治乎？将他有要捷之法，或可补前人之未发者乎？予曰：古方用人参以补肺，御米以解毒，竹沥以清痰，干姜以养血，粟米以实胃，蜜水以润燥，姜以去秽，正是此意。张鸡峰亦曰：噎当是神思间病，惟内观自养，可以治之。此言深中病情，治法亦为近理。夫噎病主于血干。夫血者阴气也，阴主静，内外两静，则脏腑之火不起，而金水二气有养，阴血自生，肠胃津液，传化合宜，何噎之有？[34p]

    There are indeed medicinal substances such as rhubarb, gypsum, bamboo shavings, glauber's salt, plantain, radix peucedani, (shiluo) salt, poria, yellow qi, reed root, and (grass tongue) loquat, which serve as assistants and facilitators. Their beginnings may be the same, but their ends vary. The disease's evil can easily lie dormant, hence it is easier to stabilize. Some inquire: can ancient formulas truly treat those suffering from dryness in the stomach? Are there other prompt methods or can we supplement what previous scholars have missed? I reply: the ancient formulas use ginseng to nourish the lung, rice to detoxify, bamboo juice to clear phlegm, dried ginger to nourish blood, corn to strengthen the stomach, honey water to moisten dryness, and ginger to eliminate impurities; this is precisely the intention. Zhang Jifeng also states: the sensation of obstruction in swallowing must be a disease of the spirit, and only through internal observation and self-nourishment can it be treated. This insight deeply understands the disease condition, and the treatment method aligns well with the principles. The condition of obstruction primarily relates to blood dryness. Blood is yin energy, which signifies stillness. When both the internal and external are still, the fire within the organs does not rise, allowing the dual energies of metal and water to nourish, leading to the spontaneous generation of yin blood. This ensures that the fluids of the intestines and stomach are properly transformed and harmonized—so how could there be any obstruction?[34p]

    　　　　证治要诀 【明　戴思恭】

    　　　　　噎膈证治

    　　诸痞塞及噎膈，乃是痰为气所激而上，气又为痰所隔而滞，痰与气搏，不能流通，并宜用二陈汤加枳实、缩砂仁各半钱，木香一钱，或五膈宽中散。应诸痞塞胀满，胸膈不利，或气上逆，或腹疼痛，并宜木香流气饮。应膈上诸般冷气，不问痞塞及疼痛，且与姜汁一二盏；痰饮尤宜。　　邪气作痞，宜用疏剂。若气不顺，逆上为痞，此乃虚痞，愈疏而痞愈作，宜于收补中微有疏通之意，不可十分用香剂。古方载，泻后痞膈用理中，即此意也。[35p]

    Key Points in Diagnosis and Treatment
    (Ming Dynasty - Dai Sigong)

    Treatment for Food Stasis

    Food stasis and esophageal obstruction are caused by phlegm being agitated by qi, and qi being obstructed by phlegm, leading to a blockage where phlegm and qi cannot flow freely. It is recommended to use Erchen Decoction with half a qian of Fructus Aurantii and Grains of Paradise, along with one qian of Saussurea. Alternatively, the Wuge Kuanzhong Powder may be used. This applies to symptoms of fullness and bloating, unjustified chest oppression, upward qi counterflow, or abdominal pain; it is also beneficial to use the Muxiang Liuqi Drink. For various cold pathogens in the chest, regardless of bloating or pain, it is good to administer one or two bowls of ginger juice, especially helpful for phlegm-damp retention.

    When evil qi causes obstruction, it is advisable to use dispersing agents. If qi is not flowing smoothly and reverses to cause obstruction, this is classified as a deficiency obstruction. The more one tries to disperse it, the more it develops; thus, it is necessary to balance tonification with a subtle approach to dispersal without excessive use of aromatic agents. According to ancient prescriptions, after purging, for treatment of bloating, the principle of regulating the center applies.[35p]

    　　因七气所伤，结滞成痰，痞塞满闷，宜四七汤，或导痰汤加木香半钱，或下来复丹。因冷气滞停，中脘痞塞，并可用挝脾汤加丁香，或丁沉透膈汤。因伤食痞塞，见伤食证，气虚上逆，遂成痞塞而疼者，六磨饮吞黑锡丹。　　若痞塞服诸药不效，大便不甚通者，宜感应丸加巴豆，或半硫丸、备急丸、木香槟榔丸通之。　　诸五噎五膈，并宜五膈宽中散；不效，谷神嘉禾散，前痞塞诸药，皆可选用。噎膈甚而水浆不入，药食皆不下，食入口即吐者，当镇坠之，宜盐汤下灵砂丹，仍以嘉禾散作末，干点服。[36p]

    Due to injury from the seven emotions, phlegm accumulates, causing pressure and fullness. One should take Siqi Decoction or Daotan Decoction with half a qian of Mu Xiang, or take Xia Lai Fu Dan. When cold qi is stagnant, causing fullness in the middle jiao, one can use Zhuapi Decoction with Clove, or Ding Chen Tou Ge Decoction. If there is food stagnation with corresponding symptoms, qi deficiency leads to counterflow and causes pain and fullness; in this case, take Liu Mo Drink or swallow He Xi Dan.

    If fullness does not improve with various medicines, and there is not severe constipation, one should take Gan Ying Pill with Ba Dou, or prepare Han Liu Pill, Bei Ji Pill, or Mu Xiang Bing Lang Pill to relieve it.

    For all forms of choking and obstruction, one should also take Wu Ge Kuan Zhong San. If this is ineffective, use Gu Shen Jia He San. Various medicines for previous fullness can also be chosen. If the obstruction is severe and neither liquids nor food can be ingested, and anything taken is immediately vomited, one should stabilize and settle this condition. It is advisable to take saltwater with Ling Sha Dan, and still use Jia He San in powdered form, taking it dry.[36p]

    　　　　　翻胃

    　　翻胃之病所以重于呕吐者，呕吐食入即吐，翻胃则或一日半日，食复翻上，不化如故。腹中非不欲食，不肯留，胃气不温，不能消食，食既不消，不为糟粕而入大肠，必随气上逆，从口而出。故翻胃人胸膈多为冷气所痞，二陈汤加丁香十粒、枳壳半钱，或治中汤加枳壳、砂仁各半钱，半夏一钱，入米与生姜同煎。　　若胃寒甚，服药而翻者，宜附子粳米汤加丁香十粒、砂仁半钱；大便秘者，更加枳壳半钱。　　若胸膈痞甚而翻，宜谷神嘉禾散，加生附一钱，或丁沉透膈汤、五膈宽中散加生附一钱；仍以来复丹升降其阴阳，通其隧道。半硫丸亦可通之。隧道久不通，名结肠翻胃，半硫丸尤宜。百药无效，势危笃者，宜桂香清金散以坠之。一法用胡椒一味，酢浸之，晒干复浸，不计遍数，愈多愈好，碾米末酢糊为丸，淡酢汤下十丸，加至三四十九。[37p]

    Reverse Stomach

    The reason the illness of reverse stomach is more serious than vomiting is that, while vomiting expels food immediately, reverse stomach may last for a day or more, with food returning undigested. The stomach does not lack the desire to eat, but is unwilling to retain food; the stomach's qi is cold and cannot digest, leading to undigested food not becoming waste and entering the large intestine, which must rise and be expelled from the mouth. Therefore, those with reverse stomach often have their chest and diaphragm oppressed by cold qi. For treatment, one may use Er Chen Decoction, adding ten grains of clove and half a qian of bitter orange peel, or Zhongzhi Decoction with half a qian each of bitter orange peel and sand seed, and one qian of half summer, boiled with rice and fresh ginger.

    If the stomach is very cold and the patient vomits after taking medicine, it is advisable to use Aconite and glutinous rice soup with ten grains of clove and half a qian of sand seed; if there is constipation, add another half qian of bitter orange peel. If the oppression in the chest and diaphragm is severe and there is reverse stomach, it is suitable to use Gu Shen Jia He Powder, adding one qian of fresh Aconite, or use Ding Chen Tuo Ge Decoction or Wu Ge Kuan Zhong Powder, also adding one qian of fresh Aconite; furthermore, use Liufu Dan to regulate yin and yang and open the passage. Half-sulfur pill can also promote passage. Long-term blockage of the passage is termed colonic reverse stomach, and the half-sulfur pill is particularly suitable.

    If all medicines prove ineffective and the condition is critical, one should use Gui Xiang Qing Jin Powder to induce a resolution. One method involves soaking pepper in vinegar, drying, and soaking it again, without counting the number of times; the more, the better. Grind it into rice powder, mix it with vinegar to form pills, and take ten pills with diluted vinegar soup, increasing to thirty or forty-nine.[37p]

    　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

    　　　　　关格证治

    　　经云：人迎脉大于气口四倍，名曰格；气口脉大于人迎四倍，名曰关。关乃阳不下，以寒在胸中，塞而不入；格乃阴不上，以热在下焦，塞而不出。上下不通，三焦撩乱，中气不足，阴阳不能相荣，故既关且格。　　中虚者，补中益气汤加槟榔以升降之。中虚痰盛者，六君子汤去朮加柏子仁及麝少许。虚甚吐利俱不得者，既济丸。　　关格与噎稍异。胃中觉气有碍，欲升不升，欲降不降，欲食不食，宜二陈汤加木通，吐其横格之气，不必在出痰也。　　古云：关格死在旦夕，但治下焦可愈。经云：少阳所至，为呕涌溢，食不下，言火逆上而为呕吐，非膈上所生独为关，非格也，大承气汤下之。若但吐而不得小便者，胃苓汤。有膏粱积热，损伤北方真水者，滋肾丸主之。忌用淡渗利水之药。凡关格见头汗者死。[38p]

    Introduction to Medicine 【Ming Dynasty, Li Zhan】

    Diagnosis of Guange (Closed Position and Blockage)

    The classic states: When the Renying pulse is four times greater than the Qikou pulse, it is called "ge" (blockage); when the Qikou pulse is four times greater than the Renying pulse, it is called "guan" (closed position). The "guan" signifies that Yang does not descend, as cold is present in the chest, blocking its entry; "ge" signifies that Yin does not ascend, as heat is present in the lower jiao, blocking its exit. When the upper and lower parts do not communicate, the three jiaos become disordered, middle qi is insufficient, and Yin and Yang cannot nourish each other, hence it is both "guan" and "ge."

    For those with middle vacuity, use "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction" with areca nut to adjust the rise and fall. For those with significant middle vacuity and phlegm accumulation, take "Liujunzi Decoction" minus the atractylodes, adding arborvitae seeds and a small amount of musk. For severe vacuity with vomiting and diarrhea where nothing can be retained, use "Jijiu Pill."

    "Guange" is slightly different from "ye" (obstruction). When there is a sensation of obstruction in the stomach, desire to ascend but unable, desire to descend but unable, desire to eat but unable, apply "Erchen Decoction" with houttuynia to expel the horizontal obstructive qi; it is not necessary to expel phlegm.

    Ancient texts say: "Guange deaths occur from morning to night, but treating the lower jiao can lead to recovery." The classics state: "When the lesser yang channels are involved, it leads to vomiting, food not being retained, indicating that heat rises and causes vomiting; it is not solely caused by obstruction above, nor is it simply a 'ge.' Use "Dachengqi Decoction" to purge it. If one vomits but cannot urinate, use "Weiling Decoction." For damp-heat accumulation affecting the true water of the north, administer "Zishen Pill." Avoid using diuretics that are bland and that facilitate water drainage. Any patient with "guange" presenting with head sweating has a fatal prognosis.[38p]

    　　　　　膈噎证治

    　　饮食不下而大便不通，名膈噎。疏云：膈有拒格意，即膈食反胃也。《玉机》云：噎塞大便不通，通幽汤。故以膈噎为题。《局方》以噎近咽，膈近胃，而遗下焦，又妄分十膈五噎，皆非经旨。病因内伤忧郁失志，及饮食淫欲，而动脾胃肝肾之火，或因杂病，误服辛香燥药，俱令血液衰耗，胃脘枯槁。其槁在上焦贲门者，食不能下，则胃脘当心而痛，须臾吐出乃止。贲门即胃脘上口，言水谷自此奔入于胃，而气则传之于肺也。其槁在中焦幽门者，食物可下，良久复出。幽门与中脘相近，言其位幽僻，胃中水谷自此而入小肠也。[39p]

    Diagnosis and Treatment of Esophageal Obstruction

    When food cannot be ingested and there is constipation, it is called esophageal obstruction. The text states: "Obstruction implies a rejection, that is, food returns to the stomach." The "Jade Machine" mentions that obstruction leads to constipation; thus, the remedy is "Tongyou Decoction." Therefore, esophageal obstruction is the subject. The "Jufang" states that obstruction is close to the throat and the diaphragm is close to the stomach, while neglecting the lower burner, misguidedly dividing obstructive issues into ten diaphragm obstructions and five esophageal obstructions, all of which deviate from the principles found in classical texts. The cause of the disease stems from internal injuries due to worries, loss of will, and excessive indulgence in food and desires, which aggravate the fire of the spleen, stomach, liver, and kidneys; or it may arise from miscellaneous illnesses, due to the improper use of spicy and drying medicines, all leading to blood and fluids depleting, and the stomach becoming dry and withered. When this dryness occurs in the upper burner (at the cardia), food cannot descend, causing pain in the stomach, which persists until vomiting occurs to relieve the suffering. The cardia is the upper opening of the stomach, where food and drink rush in, and the qi is transmitted to the lungs. When the dryness is in the middle burner (at the pylorus), food can descend, but after a while, it is expelled. The pylorus is located near the center, indicating its obscure position, where food and drink enter the small intestine.[39p]

    其槁在下焦阑门者，朝食暮吐，暮食朝吐。阑门，脐下栏约水谷，分入膀胱大肠而为粪溺，是大小肠膀胱，乃气血津液流通之道路也。　　经曰：三阳结谓之膈。小肠热结则血脉燥，大肠热结则不能便，膀胱热结则津液涸。三阳热结，脉必洪数有力，前后闭塞，下既不通，必反而上行，所以噎食不下，纵下复出，乃阳火上行而不下降也。　　实火，黄连解毒汤加童便、姜汁，或益元散入姜汁澄白脚为小丸，时时服之；温六丸尤妙。甚者，陶氏六一承气汤、人参利膈丸。　　虚火冲上食不入者，枳桔二陈汤加厚朴、白朮及木香少许，或古萸连丸。渴者，钱氏白朮散。[40p]

    The condition in the lower burner, at the threshold, manifests as morning eating and evening vomiting, or evening eating and morning vomiting. The threshold regulates the water and grains beneath the navel, dividing them into the bladder and large intestine to form feces and urine. It is the pathway for the flow of qi, blood, and fluids of the small intestine, large intestine, and bladder.

    The classics state: "The three yangs that are congealed are called the diaphragm." When there is heat blockage in the small intestine, the blood vessels become dry; when there is heat blockage in the large intestine, one cannot have a bowel movement; when there is heat blockage in the bladder, the fluids become depleted. With the three yangs blocked by heat, the pulse must be vigorous and rapid, and there will be obstruction both before and after, with blockage below leading to a counter-flow upwards, thus causing food to be stuck and inability to swallow, resulting in regurgitation. This is due to the upward movement of yang fire without descending.

    For real fire, use Huanglian Jiedu Decoction with added child's urine and ginger juice, or form into small pills with Yiyuan Powder mixed with clarified ginger juice, taking them regularly; Wenhui Six Pills are also particularly good. In severe cases, use Tao's Liuyi Chengqi Decoction or Ren Shen Li Ge Pill.

    For empty fire surging upward causing food not to enter, use Zhiji Erchen Decoction with added Houpo, Baizhu, and a little Muxiang, or Gu Yu Lian Pills. For thirst, use Qian's Baizhu Powder.[40p]

    大便闭者，导滞通幽汤，或参仁丸、麻子仁丸。当噎未至于膈之时，便宜服此防之。膏肓之疾，岂可怠忽！　　间有身受寒气，口伤冷物，以致脾胃火衰，膈上苦冷，肠鸣，脉必滑微，宜暂用丁香煮散、五膈汤、五噎汤、单附子散以劫之。若不求其本，偏认为寒，概用辛香燥药，必至烁阴不救。　　古云：膈噎神思间病，惟内观养之。盖七情火起，熏蒸津液，为痰为积，积久则血愈衰。《针经》曰：怒气所至，食则气逆不下；劳气所至，为膈噎喘促；思气所至，为中痞，三焦闭塞，咽嗌不利。[41p]

    For those suffering from constipation, one should take "Guide Stagnation and Open the Hidden Decoction," or "Shen Ren Pill" or "Ma Zi Ren Pill." When experiencing a sensation of choking not yet reaching the diaphragm, it is advisable to take these as a precaution. Can one neglect ailments affecting the vital center?

    Sometimes, the body receives cold air, or the mouth is hurt by cold substances, leading to diminished spleen and stomach fire, a feeling of bitterness and cold above the diaphragm, intestinal rumbling, and a pulse that must be slippery and weak; it is appropriate to temporarily use "Clove Boiled Powder," "Five Diaphragm Decoction," "Five Choking Decoction," or "Single Aconite Powder" to alleviate this. If one does not seek the root cause and instead believes it to be merely cold, using pungent and drying medications indiscriminately will inevitably damage the yin without providing relief.

    The ancients said: Choking in the diaphragm relates to the spirit, and only inner observation can nurture it. As emotions ignite fire, they evaporate fluids, generating phlegm and accumulation; prolonged accumulation leads to weakening blood. The "Needle Classic" states: When anger arises, food cannot descend properly; when fatigued energy arises, it results in choking, wheezing, and shortness of breath; when thinking too much, it leads to fullness in the center and obstruction in the triple warmer, causing difficulty in swallowing.[41p]

    　　痰饮，脉滑或伏，二陈汤、古参夏汤、化痰丸、(艹舌)蒌实丸，或用黄连、吴萸、贝母、(艹舌)蒌仁、牛转草，水煎。　　食积，脉滑而短，枳朮丸加黄连、陈皮、半夏，或狗米平胃丸、虎脂平胃丸，或用保和丸二钱，加姜炒黄连三钱、山楂二钱为丸，麻仁大胭脂为衣，每六十丸，人参煎汤，入竹沥下。　　七情郁结，脉沉而濇，饮食喜静，胸背痛者，四七汤、温胆汤；痞满烦闷微嗽，二便不利者，分心气饮、四磨汤，或木香、槟榔二味等分为末，白汤下；伤神不睡者，十味温胆汤、朱砂安神丸；腹胀肠鸣者，木香匀气散；有积聚者，阿魏撞气丸；恶闻食气者，五膈宽中散。　　气血两虚，口沫大出者，死。[42p]

    Phlegm and fluid retention, with a slippery or hidden pulse, can be treated with Er Chen Tang, Gu Shen Xia Tang, Hua Tan Wan, or (caltrop) Luo Shi Wan. Alternatively, one may use Huang Lian, Wu Yu, Bei Mu, (caltrop) Luo Ren, and Niu Zuan Cao, decocted in water.

    For food accumulation, with a slippery and short pulse, Zhi Jun Wan can be enhanced with Huang Lian, Chen Pi, and Ban Xia, or treated with Gou Mi Ping Wei Wan or Hu Zhi Ping Wei Wan. Alternatively, one can use Bao He Wan (two qian), and add ginger-fried Huang Lian (three qian) and Shan Zha (two qian) to form pills, coated with Ma Ren Da Yan Zhi. For every sixty pills, steep in ginseng decoction, mixed with bamboo juice.

    For emotional stagnation causing a deep and rough pulse, preferring stillness in food, and pain in the chest and back, use Si Qi Tang or Wen Dan Tang. If there is discomfort and slight cough with difficulty in urination, use Fen Xin Qi Yin or Si Mo Tang, or prepare a powder of equal parts Mu Xiang and Bing Lang to take with warm water. For those disturbed and unable to sleep, use Shi Wei Wen Dan Tang or Zhu Sha An Shen Wan. For abdominal distension and intestinal rumbling, use Mu Xiang Yun Qi San. In case of accumulation, employ A Wei Zhuang Qi Wan; for aversion to food odors, use Wu Ge Kuan Zhong San.

    In cases of both qi and blood deficiency, with excessive salivation, the prognosis is poor.[42p]

    　　气虚不能运化生痰者，脉必缓而无力，四君子汤。大便闭，加芦根、童便；气虚甚者，六君子汤加附子、大黄；酒毒，加甘蔗汁。单人参汤、人参膏尤妙。　　血虚不能滋润生火者，脉必数而无力，四物汤加童便、竹沥、姜汁。大便闭，加桃仁、红花；有瘀血，加牡丹皮、韭汁；防生虫，加驴尿；血虚甚，加干姜；血燥，加牛羊乳汁。不可以人乳代之，盖人乳反有七情饮食之毒火故也。　　气血俱虚者，八物汤主之。[43p]

    If there is a deficiency of qi that cannot manage and transform phlegm, the pulse will be slow and weak; use the Four Gentlemen Decoction. If there is constipation, add reed root and child's urine; if the qi deficiency is severe, use the Six Gentlemen Decoction with aconite and rhubarb; for alcohol toxicity, add sugarcane juice. The single ginseng decoction and ginseng paste are especially effective.

    If there is a deficiency of blood that cannot nourish the body and generate fire, the pulse will be rapid and weak; use the Four Substance Decoction with child's urine, bamboo sap, and ginger juice. For constipation, add peach kernel and safflower; if there is stagnant blood, add peony root and leek juice; to prevent parasites, add donkey urine; if the blood deficiency is severe, add dried ginger; if the blood is dry, add cow or sheep milk. Human milk should not be used in place of this, because human milk may contain toxic fire from emotions and diet.

    For those with both qi and blood deficiency, the Eight Substance Decoction is indicated.[43p]

    　　血阴主静，内外两静，则脏腑之火不起，而金水二气有养，阴血自生，津液传化合宜，何膈噎之有！　　大概不问虚实，俱以益阴养胃为主，庶免后患，或肾气丸主之。　　通用二陈汤加童便、竹沥、姜汁、韭汁。有热加酒炒芩连、(艹舌)蒌、桔梗，七情加香附、川芎、木香、槟榔，不纳食加麦芽、神曲，热结食返上奔，加大黄、桃仁，气虚合四君子汤，血虚合四物汤。　　杂方：烧针丸、杵糠丸、紫金锭、霞天膏、神仙夺命丹、古阿魏散，或灵砂烧酒下。凡五十岁后血枯，粪如羊屎，及年少不淡薄饮食，断绝房室者，不治。[44p]

    When the blood and yin are tranquil, both internally and externally, the fire of the organs does not rise, allowing the energies of metal and water to nourish. The yin blood will naturally thrive, and the fluids will transform and harmonize appropriately, so how can there be any obstruction or discomfort?

    Generally, regardless of deficiency or excess, the focus should be on nourishing yin and supporting the stomach to prevent future issues, or the usage of Kidney Qi Pills.

    A commonly used formula is Er Chen Tang with additions of children's urine, bamboo juice, ginger juice, and chive juice. If there is heat, add fried Qianlian, (chuan)lian, and Platycodon; for emotional disturbances, add Xiangfu, Chuanxiong, Muxiang, and Betel Nut. If digestion is poor, add malt and shenqu; if there is food stasis causing reverse flow, add Da Huang and Tao Ren. For qi deficiency, use Si Jun Zi Tang; for blood deficiency, use Si Wu Tang.

    Miscellaneous prescriptions include Shou Zhen Wan, Chu Cang Wan, Zijing Ding, Xiatian Gao, Shenxian Duoming Dan, and Gu Awei San, or use Ling Sha with light wine.

    Those over fifty with dried blood, whose stools resemble sheep dung, and younger individuals with heavy food intake or who have stopped sexual activities, should not be treated.[44p]

    　　　　　反胃证治

    　　胃冷呕青，手足厥，食久乃吐，二陈汤加姜桂，甚加丁附，或丁香半夏丸。　　胃热面红，手足热，食已即吐，二陈加姜炒芩连、山栀。暴甚，略加槟榔、木香，胃口痛，加姜汁，或葛根竹茹汤、加味橘皮竹茹汤，或小柴胡汤加竹茹；如时常口吐清水，冷涎自下涌上者，此脾热所致也。二陈汤加白朮、白芍、升麻、炒芩连、山栀、神曲、麦芽、干生姜等分，或丸或煎服。　　凡气吐者气冲胸痛，食已暴吐而渴，始当降气和中，六君子汤加木香、藿香、桔梗、枇杷叶，或七气汤；热气冲者，古荆黄汤加人参、甘草、煨姜。
    　　　　医宗必读 【明　李中梓】[45p]

    Treatment of Nausea and Vomiting

    For cold in the stomach causing blue vomiting, with cold extremities, and vomiting long after eating, use Erchen Decoction with added ginger and cinnamon, or Dingxiang Banxia Pill.

    For heat in the stomach with a flushed face, warm extremities, and vomiting immediately after eating, use Erchen Decoction with stir-fried Scutellaria and gardenia. If severe, add betel nut and agarwood. For stomach pain, add ginger juice; alternatively, use Ge Gen Zhu Ru Decoction or a modified tangerine peel and bamboo shavings decoction, or Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with bamboo shavings. If there is frequent vomiting of clear water, leading to cold phlegm rising from below, this is caused by heat in the spleen. Use Erchen Decoction with white poria, white peony, Cimicifuga, stir-fried Scutellaria and gardenia, Shenqu, malt, and dried ginger in equal parts, either as pills or decoction.

    For vomiting due to qi rising, causing chest pain, or forceful vomiting immediately after eating with thirst, one should first calm the qi and harmonize the middle. Use Six Gentleman Decoction with added agarwood, patchouli, platycodon, and loquat leaves, or Seven Qi Decoction. If it is heat qi rising, use Ancient Jinghuang Decoction with ginseng, licorice, and simmered ginger.

    Medical Canon Must-Reads

    【Ming Dynasty, Li Zhongzi】[45p]

    　　　　　反胃噎塞

    　　按反胃噎膈，总是血液衰耗，胃脘干槁。槁在上者，水饮可行，食物难入，名曰噎塞；槁在下者，食虽可入，良久复出，名曰反胃。二证总名为膈，故《内经》止有三阳结谓之膈一语。洁古分吐证为三端：上焦吐者皆从于气，食则暴吐；中焦吐者，皆从于积，或先吐而痛，或先痛而吐；下焦吐者，皆从于寒，朝食暮吐，暮食朝吐。巢氏浪分五噎十膈，支派烦多，惑人滋甚。惟张鸡峰以为神思间病，法当内观静养，斯言深中病情。大抵气血亏损，复因悲思忧恚，则脾胃受伤，血液渐耗，郁气生痰，痰则塞而不通，气则上而不下，妨碍道路，饮食难进，噎塞所由成也。脾胃虚伤，运行失职，不能熟腐五谷，变化精微，朝食暮吐，暮食朝吐，食虽入胃，复反而出，反胃所由成也。二者皆在膈间受病，故通名为膈也。噎塞之吐，即洁古之上焦吐；反胃之吐，即洁古之下焦吐。王太仆云：食不得入，是有火也；食入反出，是无火也。[46p]

    Nausea and Dysphagia

    Nausea and dysphagia are fundamentally due to the depletion of blood and the dryness of the stomach. When dryness is in the upper part, fluids can pass, but food is difficult to enter, hence it is called dysphagia; when the dryness is in the lower part, food may enter but is later expelled after a long time, hence it is called nausea. Both conditions are generally referred to as "the diaphragm," which is why the "Inner Canon" only mentions "the diaphragm" as a term for the three yang blockages. According to ancient texts, there are three kinds of vomiting: vomiting from the upper jiao is due to qi, where food leads to violent vomiting; vomiting from the middle jiao is due to accumulation, sometimes preceded by pain or followed by pain after vomiting; vomiting from the lower jiao is due to cold, where morning food is expelled in the evening and evening food in the morning.

    Cao's school divides the symptoms into five types of dysphagia and ten types of diaphragm conditions, which makes the categorization overly complex and confusing. Only Zhang Jifeng suggests that such illness arises from within one's own contemplation and requires inner observation and quiet nurturing, which deeply resonates with the condition of illness. Generally speaking, the depletion of qi and blood, compounded by sadness, worry, and anger, injures the spleen and stomach, gradually depleting the blood, causing stagnant qi to generate phlegm, which then blocks and obstructs pathways, making it difficult for food and drink to enter—this results in dysphagia. When the spleen and stomach are weakly injured and lose their functions, they are unable to properly digest grains and transform them into essences. Thus, morning food is expelled in the evening and evening food in the morning; although food may enter the stomach, it will return and be rejected—this is how nausea arises. Both conditions occur in the area of the diaphragm, hence the common designation as "the diaphragm." The vomiting associated with dysphagia corresponds to the upper jiao vomiting in ancient texts; the vomiting associated with nausea corresponds to the lower jiao vomiting. Wang Taibu states: if food cannot enter, it indicates the presence of heat; if food enters and then is expelled, it indicates the absence of heat.[46p]

    噎塞大都属热，反胃大都属寒。然亦不可拘也。脉大有力，当作热治；脉小无力，当作寒医。色之黄白而枯者为虚寒；色之红赤而泽者为实热。以脉合证，以色合脉，庶乎无误。经曰：能合色脉，可以万全。此证之所以疑难者，方欲健脾理痰，恐燥剂有妨于津液；方欲养血生津，恐润剂有碍于中州。审其阴伤火旺者，当以养血为亟；脾伤阴盛者，当以温补为先。[47p]

    Generally, obstruction and choking predominantly relate to heat, while nausea usually corresponds to cold. However, one should not be overly rigid in this approach. If the pulse is strong and large, one should treat it as heat; if the pulse is weak and small, it should be treated as cold. A yellowish-white complexion that appears withered indicates deficiency and cold; a reddish complexion that is lustrous indicates excess and heat. By correlating the pulse with symptoms and the complexion with the pulse, one can avoid errors. As the classics state: "Those who can unite color and pulse can achieve completeness."
