    然下之不通，又何非上气之不化乎？盖脾胃气虚，然后治节不行，而无以生血，血涸于下，所以结闭不行，此真阴枯槁证也。必使血气渐充，脏腑渐润，方是救本之治。若徒为目前计而推之逐之，则虽见暂通而真阴愈竭矣。故治此之法，但见其阴虚兼寒者，宜以补阳为主，而大加当归、肉苁蓉、韭汁、姜汁之属；阴虚兼热者，宜以补阴为主，而加乳汁、童便、酥油、蜂蜜、豕膏、诸血之属。然此等证治，取效最难，万勿欲速，非加以旬月功夫，安心调理，不能愈也！其有粪如羊矢，或年高病此者，尤为难治。　　反胃由于酒湿伤脾者，宜葛花解酲汤主之。若湿多成热，而见胃火上冲者，宜黄芩汤或半夏泻心汤之类主之。[90p]

    If the lower passages are obstructed, how can it not be a reflection of the upper energy not transforming? It is because the spleen and stomach have weakened qi; thus, the cycle of circulation does not function, and there is insufficient blood production, leading to a stagnation below which causes blockage. This is a true manifestation of desiccation of the yin. It is essential to gradually nourish the blood and qi and moisten the internal organs, as this is the fundamental treatment. If one merely seeks immediate results without addressing the root cause, there may be temporary relief, but the true yin will become further depleted. Therefore, in treating this condition, if one observes deficiency of yin along with cold, the main approach should be to tonify the yang, significantly incorporating ingredients like angelica, cistanche, leek juice, and ginger juice. If there is deficiency of yin accompanied by heat, the main approach should be to nourish the yin, adding substances like milk, children's urine, ghee, honey, pig fat, and various types of blood. However, these treatments are particularly difficult to yield results, and one must not desire quick fixes. Without a period of careful adjustment, usually spanning several weeks or months, recovery cannot be achieved! Conditions presenting with feces resembling sheep droppings, or those who are older and suffer from this ailment, are especially challenging to treat. For instances of reversed stomach due to alcohol dampening the spleen, the main prescription should be Ge Hua Jie Cheng Decoction. If there is excess dampness leading to heat, with symptoms of stomach fire surging upwards, Huang Qin Decoction or Ban Xia Xie Xin Decoction should be administered.[90p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　噎膈反胃治法

    　　反胃证初起之时，未尝非胃病也，当时以逍遥散加黄连一钱立止。无如世医不知治法，乃用香砂、厚朴、枳壳、砂仁之类，纷投之不应；又改用大黄、巴豆之类下之，又不应；改用黄连、黄蘗、黄芩、栀子、知母大寒之品以凉之，又不应；改用桂枝、白果、肉桂、附子、干姜、吴茱萸之类以热之，又不应；始用柴胡、荆芥、桔梗、防风、苏子之类以散之，遂成噎膈之证矣。吾今传一方，用熟地一两，山茱萸四钱，麦冬三钱，北五味、元参、当归、白芥子各一钱，牛膝二钱，水煎服。此方之妙，全在不治反胃，正所以治反胃也。盖人反胃，乃是肾中阴水竭也，肾水不足则大肠细小，水不足以润之，故肠细而干涸。肠既细小，则饮食入胃，不能下行，必反而上吐。治之之法，不可治上，宜治下。[91p]

    Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber
    [Qing Dynasty - Chen Shiduo]

    Treatment Method for Reflux and Nausea

    At the onset of reflux symptoms, it is not necessarily a stomach issue. At this point, taking Xiao Yao San with ten grams of Huai Lian can stop it. However, many doctors do not understand the treatment method and instead use ingredients like Xiang Sha, Hou Po, Zhi Ke, and Sha Ren, which do not work; they then switch to using Da Huang and Ba Dou, which also fail. Next, they try cooling herbs like Huang Lian, Huang Bo, Huang Qin, Zhi Zi, and Zhi Mu, but this too is ineffective. They try warming herbs such as Gui Zhi, Bai Guo, Rou Gui, Fu Zi, Gan Jiang, and Wu Zhu Yu, yet there is still no response. Finally, they use dispersing herbs like Chai Hu, Jing Jie, Jie Geng, Fang Feng, and Su Zi, resulting in the condition of reflux.

    Now, I pass on a formula: one ounce of Shu Di, four coins of Shan Zhu Yu, three coins of Mai Dong, one coin each of Bei Wu Wei, Yuan Shen, Dang Gui, and Bai Jie Zi, and two coins of Niu Xi, boiled in water for consumption. The brilliance of this formula lies in not treating the reflux directly, which is precisely how to treat it. The reason for reflux is the depletion of Yin water in the kidneys. When kidney water is insufficient, the large and small intestines cannot be sufficiently moistened, leading to dryness. With dry intestines, food entering the stomach cannot descend and must instead be vomited back up. Therefore, the method of treatment should not focus on the upper part but rather on the lower.[91p]

    方用熟地、山茱萸之类，纯是补肾中之水也，肾水足而大肠有水相资，则大肠仍复宽转，可以容物，水路既宽，则舟楫无碍，大舸小舶，可以顺行，又何惧区区小舟不可以转运粮食哉？此肾中虚而水不足以润大肠者，宜如是治法。若肾中寒凉而虚者，又不如是治也。盖反胃之名虽同，反胃之实各异。肾中无水而反胃者，食下喉即吐；肾中无火而反胃者，食久而始吐也。譬如今日食之，明日始尽将今日之物吐出也。方用熟地一两，山茱萸四钱，麦冬三钱，山药、茯苓各二钱，北五味、丹皮、泽泻、牛膝、附子、肉桂各一钱，水煎服。此方八味丸汤也。妙在用附子、肉桂于补肾水之中，使去水中补火。补火者补命门之火也。盖脾胃之气，必得命门之火始生，譬如釜下无火，何以煮爨？未免水冷金寒，结成冰冻，必得一阳初复之气始解。[92p]

    The formula employs prepared rehmannia and shan zhu yu, which are purely for replenishing the water in the kidneys. When kidney water is sufficient, the large intestine is also nourished with water, allowing it to expand and properly accommodate substances. When the pathway for water is wide, boats of all sizes can navigate freely; hence, there is no fear that a small boat cannot transport grain. This treatment is appropriate for a deficiency of water in the kidneys that fails to moisten the large intestine. However, if the kidneys are cold and deficient, this method is not suitable. Although the name "reversal of stomach" may be the same, the actual condition differs. Reversal due to a lack of water in the kidneys causes immediate vomiting upon swallowing food, while reversal from a lack of fire in the kidneys results in delayed vomiting, where food is retained until the next day before being expelled. For example, food eaten today may only be vomited out the next day.

    The formula includes one tael of prepared rehmannia, four qian of shan zhu yu, three qian of mai dong, two qian each of shan yao and fu ling, one qian each of northern wuweizi, dan pi, ze xie, niu xi, fu zi, and rou gui, and is decocted in water for consumption. This is the eight-ingredient pill soup. The key lies in using fu zi and rou gui to nourish kidney water while also addressing the fire within the water. Nourishing the fire helps to rejuvenate the life-gate fire. The qi of the spleen and stomach must rely on the life-gate fire to be generated; like a pot without fire, how can it cook? Without it, the water is cold and metal is chilled, leading to frost. One must first restore the initial warmth of yang to resolve this.[92p]

    人身脾胃亦然，然而寒凉之病，止该腹痛心疼，今反无此证，乃上越而吐者何也？盖脾胃有出路，则寒邪之气不留于中。今日日上吐，将胃口咽门已成大道，熟径往来，无所阻滞，则径情趋奔，其势甚便，又何必积蓄于中州，盘踞于心腹，发寒作热，以苦楚此脾胃哉？此反胃下寒，心腹之所以不痛也。此又不治反胃而适所以治反胃，此变法治病之端也。　　有食入而即出者，此肾水虚不能润喉，故喉燥而即出也。有食久而反出者，此肾火虚不能温脾，故脾寒而反出也。治反胃者，但当治肾，但当辨其有火无火之异，则死证可变为生也。治反胃之证，莫妙用仲景地黄汤。但无火者，加附子、肉桂，则效验如向。然人亦有用仲景方而不验者，何也？以用之不得其法，而非方之不神也。今酌定二方，一治无火而反胃者：熟地一两，山茱萸一两，附子、茯苓、泽泻、丹皮、肉桂各三钱，山药一钱，水煎服。[93p]

    The human body’s spleen and stomach function similarly; however, in the case of illnesses caused by cold and chill, one usually experiences abdominal pain and distress. Yet, if there are no such symptoms now, what could be the reason for the upward sensation accompanied by vomiting? It is because when the spleen and stomach have a passage, the cold pathogenic energy does not remain within. Now, with the upward forces releasing through the mouth and throat, the gastric entrance has become a broad avenue, allowing for free passage without obstruction. Thus, the energy easily flows, and there is no need for it to accumulate within the central region, lurking in the heart and abdomen, causing cold to generate heat that brings suffering to the spleen and stomach. This, in fact, is what allows for the absence of pain in the heart and abdomen. This is not merely about treating the symptoms of vomiting but rather addressing the root cause of it; this marks the beginning of transformative methods for treating diseases.

    When food enters and quickly exits, it is due to the deficiency of kidney water, which fails to moisten the throat, leading to dryness and an immediate expulsion. When food lingers and then is expelled, it is due to the deficiency of kidney fire, which cannot warm the spleen, resulting in cold in the spleen and subsequent expulsion. To treat the symptoms of vomiting, it is essential to address the kidneys and to differentiate whether there is fire or no fire; doing so can transform potentially fatal symptoms into life-sustaining outcomes. The ideal remedy for the symptoms of vomiting is to use Zhang Jing’s Rehmannia Decoction. If there is no fire, one should add Aconite and Cinnamon, which will yield beneficial results just as before. However, some people may use Zhang Jing’s prescriptions without achieving results. Why is this? It is due to improperly applying the method, rather than any deficiency in the formulas themselves. Now, regarding the two prescriptions: one for treating vomiting without fire includes one ounce of cooked Rehmannia, one ounce of Sichuan Cornelian cherry, and three qian each of Aconite, Poria, Water Plantain, Moutan Peony, and Cinnamon, along with one qian of Chinese Yam, to be decocted and consumed.[93p]

    一治有火而反胃者：熟地二两，山药一两，泽泻、丹皮各三钱，茯苓、麦冬、山茱萸各五钱，北五味二钱，水煎服。二方出入加减，自然治反胃有神功也。　　反胃之证，虽一时不能遽死，然治之不得其宜，亦必死而后已。反胃多是肾虚无火，故今日食之，至明日尽吐，即《内经》所谓食人即出者是也。夫食入于胃而吐出，似乎病在胃也。谁知肾为胃之关门，肾病而胃始病。饮食之入于胃，必得肾水以相济，而咽喉有水道之通，始上可输挽，下易运化。然而肾中无火，则釜底无薪，又何以蒸水谷乎？此肾寒而脾亦寒，脾寒不能化，必上涌于胃而胃不肯受，则涌而上吐矣。方用定胃汤，熟地三两，山莱萸二两，肉桂、茯苓各三钱，水煎服。一剂而吐止，十剂而病全愈。然此治朝入暮吐，暮服朝吐者也。倘食下即吐，又不可用肉桂。加麦冬一两、北五味子一钱，亦未尝不效应如向。盖二方全是大补肾中之水火，而不去治胃，胜于治胃也。[94p]

    For treating fire and regurgitation, use: 2 taels of cooked rehmannia, 1 tael of yam, 3 qian each of alisma and processed moutan root, 5 qian each of poria, ophiopogon, and cornelian cherry, and 2 qian of northen schisandra, decoct in water and take. Adjustments can be made to this formula naturally, effectively treating regurgitation.

    The symptoms of regurgitation, though not immediately fatal, if treated improperly, can lead to death. Regurgitation is often due to kidney deficiency without fire. Therefore, if food is eaten today, it may be vomited by tomorrow, as stated in the "Inner Canon" that food consumes the person then exits. Food entering the stomach and then being vomited seems like a stomach problem. However, the kidneys serve as the gatekeeper for the stomach; if the kidneys are ill, the stomach will also become ill. For food to enter the stomach, it must be aided by kidney fluids, and the throat must have pathways for moisture to enable proper digestion.

    Without fire in the kidneys, there is no fuel for the pot, so how can it steam the water and grain? This leads to cold in the kidneys and spleen; a cold spleen cannot transform food, causing it to rise to the stomach, which cannot accept it, resulting in vomiting. The formula for settling the stomach includes: 3 taels of cooked rehmannia, 2 taels of cornelian cherry, 3 qian each of cinnamon and poria, decoct in water and take. One dose can stop vomiting, and ten can completely cure the illness. This treatment is for those who vomit from morning to night, and for those who vomit right after meals, do not use cinnamon. Instead, add 1 tael of ophiopogon and 1 qian of northen schisandra; this adjustment has proven effective. Both formulas are great for nourishing the water and fire in the kidneys without directly treating the stomach, proving to be more effective than treating the stomach itself.[94p]

    　　　　方

    　　大半夏汤 【仲景，下同】 　治胃反呕吐。　　半夏二升，洗　人参三两　白蜜一升　　右三味，以水一斗二升，和蜜，扬之二百四十遍，煮药取二升半，温服一升余，分再服。

    　　半夏一升　生姜半斤
    　　右二味，以水七升，煮取一升半，分温再服。[95p]

    Prescription

    Major Banxia Decoction (Zhongjing, same below) treats gastric reversal and vomiting. Use two sheng of Banxia, three liang of Ren Shen, and one sheng of honey. Take these three ingredients, add twelve sheng of water, mix with honey, and stir for two hundred forty times. Boil the medicine to yield two and a half sheng, warm and take one sheng, dividing into two doses.

    Minor Banxia Decoction treats vomiting where food cannot be retained. Use one sheng of Banxia and half a jin of fresh ginger. Take these two ingredients, add seven sheng of water, boil to yield one and a half sheng, and take warm in two doses.[95p]

    　　五噎圆 【《千金方》，下同】 　治胸中久寒呕逆，逆气饮食不下，结气不消。　　干姜　蜀椒　食茱萸　桂心　人参各五分　细辛　白朮　茯苓　附子各四分　橘皮六分　　右十味为末，蜜和丸如梧子大，以酒服三丸，日三。不止，稍加至十丸。　　又方　治五种之气皆令人噎。
    　　人参　半夏　桂心　防风一作防葵　小草　附子　细辛　甘草各二两　紫菀　干姜　食茱萸　芍药　乌头各六分　枳实一两　　右十四味为末，蜜丸梧子大，酒服五丸，日三。不止，加至十五丸。乌头与半夏相反，但去一味合之。[96p]

    Dahuang Gancao Decoction: Treats those who vomit immediately after eating.
    Ingredients: 4 liang of Dahuang, 1 liang of Gancao.
    Preparation: Combine both ingredients with 3 sheng of water, boil to obtain 1 sheng, and take in two warm doses.

    Fuling Zexie Decoction: Treats thirst and desire to drink water after stomach issues.
    Ingredients: 0.5 jin of Fuling, 4 liang each of Zexie and fresh ginger, 3 liang of Baizhu, 2 liang each of Gui Zhi and Gancao.
    Preparation: Boil the six ingredients in 10 dou of water to obtain 3 sheng, then add Zexie and boil again to get 2.5 sheng. Take 8 he warm three times a day.

    Wuyeyuan: Treats prolonged cold in the chest leading to nausea, reverse flow of qi affecting appetite, and stubborn qi stagnation.
    Ingredients: 0.5 liang each of dried ginger, Sichuan pepper, Shanzhuyu, and heart of cinnamon, 5 fen each of Ginseng, Fuxi, Baizhu, Poria, and 4 fen of Ziziphus; 6 fen of tangerine peel.
    Preparation: Grind all ten ingredients into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of wutong seeds; take three pills with wine three times a day. If ineffective, gradually increase to ten pills.

    Another Formula: Treats five types of qi that cause choking.
    Ingredients: 2 liang each of Ginseng, Banxia, and heart of cinnamon, 2 liang of Fangfeng, 2 liang of a small herb, 2 liang of Fuxi, 2 liang of Xixin, 2 liang of Gancao; 6 fen of Zihuan and dried ginger, 6 fen of Shanzhuyu, 6 fen of Baishao, 6 fen of Wutou; 1 liang of Zhi Shi.
    Preparation: Grind all fourteen ingredients into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of wutong seeds; take five pills with wine three times a day. If ineffective, increase to fifteen pills. Wutou and Banxia counteract each other, so just omit one ingredient for the combination.[96p]

    Bamboo Skin Decoction treats inability to speak due to choking.

    Ingredients: Bamboo skin (also known as bamboo leaves), dried ginger, each 2 liang; licorice, fresh ginger,通草 (tongcao), ginseng, poria, ephedra, five-flavor fruit, cinnamon heart, each 1 liang.

    Preparation: Grind the ten ingredients together, using 10 dou of water to cook the bamboo skin until it reduces by 2 sheng. Remove the bamboo skin, add the remaining ingredients, cook to yield 3 sheng, and divide into three doses.

    Dried Ginger Decoction treats choking from eating and drinking, also called Banxia Decoction.

    Ingredients: Dried ginger, gypsum, each 4 liang; banxia, wheat, each 1 sheng; ginseng, cinnamon heart, loofah root, each 2 liang; licorice 1 liang; Wu zhu yu 2 sheng; 30 red beans.

    Preparation: Grind the ten ingredients together, using 5 sheng of wine and 20 dou of water, cooking with 20 dates. After straining, combine the decoction and reduce to 3 sheng, and divide into three doses.

    Qi Unblocking Decoction treats fullness in the chest with choking.

    Ingredients: Banxia 8 liang; fresh ginger 6 liang; cinnamon heart 3 liang; 30 jujubes.

    Preparation: Grind the four ingredients together, using 8 sheng of water to cook until yielding 3 sheng, and divide into five doses, taken three times during the day and twice at night.

    Antelope Horn Decoction treats unyielding choking, preventing food intake.

    Ingredients: Antelope horn, 通草 (tongcao), tangerine peel, each 2 liang; magnolia bark, Wu zhu yu, dried ginger, each 3 liang; five black codonopsis roots.

    Preparation: Grind the seven ingredients together, using 9 sheng of water to cook until yielding 3 sheng, and divide into three doses, taken three times a day.

    Reversal Food Method treats empty stomach causing regurgitation, resulting in immediate vomiting.[97p]

    Ren Shen (ginseng) 1 tael, Ze Xie (alisma) 2 taels, Gan Cao ( licorice) 2 taels, Gui Xin (cinnamon) 2 taels, Ju Pi (orange peel) 3 taels, Gan Jiang (dried ginger) 3 taels, Fu Ling (poria) 4 taels, Da Huang (rhubarb) 6 taels, Zhu Ru (bamboo shavings) 5 taels.

    Take these nine ingredients, chop them, and add 8 sheng (a measure of liquid), boil down to 3 sheng. Take 7 he (a measure of liquid) per dose, three times a day and once at night. If diarrhea occurs, stop using Da Huang.

    Another prescription treats rebellious stomach qi and thirst:
    Fu Ling, Ze Xie, and Ban Xia (pinellia), each 4 taels; Gui Xin and Gan Cao, each 2 taels. Chop these five ingredients, add 5 sheng water, boil down to 2 sheng, and divide into three doses. One version adds 4 taels of Sheng Jiang (fresh ginger).

    Another prescription treats stomach rebelliousness, where food is not digested, causing continuous vomiting:
    Ren Shen, Ze Xie, and Gui Xin, each 2 taels; Fu Ling 4 taels; Ju Pi, Gan Cao, and Huang Qi (astragalus), each 3 taels; Da Huang 1.5 taels; Sheng Jiang 8 taels; Ban Xia 1 sheng; Mai Men Dong (ophiopogon) 3 sheng.

    Chop these eleven ingredients, add 12 sheng water, boil down to 3 sheng and 2 he, take 8 he per dose, three times a day and once at night. For weak individuals, take it in six doses. If diarrhea occurs, stop using Da Huang.

    Another prescription treats stomach counterflow, with morning food and evening vomiting, sharp abdominal pain after eating, due to prolonged exposure to cold:
    Ju Pi 3 taels; Gan Cao, Hou Po (magnolia bark), Fu Ling, Gui Xin, Xi Xin (asarum), Xing Ren (apricot kernels), and Zhu Pi (bamboo skin), each 2 taels; Bing Lang (betel nut) 10 pieces, Qian Hu (peucedanum) 8 taels; Sheng Jiang 5 taels; Ren Shen 1 tael.

    Chop these twelve ingredients, add 13 sheng water, boil down to 3 sheng, and divide into three doses. One version includes 2 taels of Gan Pi (sweet orange peel).[98p]

    　　华佗方　治胃反。胃反为病，朝食暮吐，心下坚如杯升，往来寒热，四逆不下食，此为关上寒澼所作，将成肺痿。　　真珠　明雄黄　丹砂各三两　(石卜)硝五两　干姜十累　　右五味为末，蜜丸如梧子，先食服三丸。若小烦者，饮水自解。然无所忌，神良无比。一方用桂心一两。[99p]

    Three taels of dried orange peel, two taels each of white atractylodes and ginseng, one tael of cinnamon bark, one hundred and twenty grains of Sichuan pepper, and one handful of garlic chives. Combine these six ingredients and grind them; soak in two sheng of water overnight. Stuff into the stomach of a sheep and sew it up. Boil in three sheng of water until the water is reduced. Strain and discard the dregs; divide into three doses.

    Another recipe for treating gastroesophageal reflux. Four taels of seemed mallow, four taels of fresh ginger, one tael of donkey-hide gelatin, five he of hemp seeds, three taels of dried orange peel, three inches of cinnamon bark, five inches of licorice, ten jujubes, and four he of evodia. Grind these nine ingredients and boil in three sheng of water and two sheng of wine to reduce to one sheng and seven he; divide into two doses.

    Hua Tuo's formula for treating stomach reflux. Stomach reflux as a sickness manifests as morning food expulsion in the evening, with a hard sensation under the heart like a cup or bowl, alternating cold and heat, and cold hands and feet not retaining food. This is caused by cold dampness in the stomach and will lead to consumption of the lungs. Combine three taels each of pearl, realgar, and cinnabar, with five taels of natron and ten pieces of dried ginger. Grind these five ingredients into a powder, form into pills the size of jujubes, and take three pills before meals. If feeling slight distress, drink water to relieve it. There are no restrictions; the effects are unparalleled. An alternative involves using one tael of cinnamon bark.[99p]

    　　柏子仁汤

    　　人参　麝香　片脑各少许

    Ingredients: Ginseng, Pinellia, White Poria, Aged Tangerine Peel, a little fragrant musk (ground separately), Cypress Seed, honey-fried Licorice.

    Jia Wei Ma Ren Wan treats obstruction of the bowels and urinary difficulty.

    Zao Jiao San treats the obstruction of bowel movements and urination lasting three to five days.
    Burn da zao jiao to a charred state.
    The above is ground into powder and taken with rice soup. Additionally, cook one tael of pig fat until done, and consume it along with its juice and fat; also take Ba Zheng San with added bing lang, zhi ke, (shi bo) xiao, tao ren, deng xin cao, and tea roots.

    Xiang Sha Kuan Zhong Tang treats qi stagnation causing chest fullness and symptoms of choking, or stomach cold pain.

    　　厚朴丸　治翻胃吐逆，饮食噎塞，气上冲心，腹中诸疾。　　厚朴　蜀椒去目微炒　川乌炮去皮，各一两半　紫菀　吴茱萸洗　菖蒲　柴胡　桔梗　茯苓　官桂　皂角去皮弦炙　干姜炮　人参各二两　黄连二两半　巴豆霜半两　　右为细末，入巴豆霜匀炼蜜为剂，旋旋丸如桐子大，每服三丸，渐次加至五七丸，以利为度，生姜汤下，食后而卧。此药治效与《局方》温白丸同，及治处暑以后秋冬间下痢大效。春夏加黄连二两，秋冬再加厚朴二两。

    Hou Po Wan treats vomit and reversal of the stomach, food obstruction, ascending qi troubling the heart, and various abdominal ailments.

    Ingredients:

    • Hou Po (Magnolia bark)
    • Shu Jiao (Sichuan pepper), lightly roasted and removed seeds, each 1.5 taels
    • Chuan Wu (Aconite), processed and peeled, 1.5 taels
    • Zi Wan (Aster),
    • Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia), washed,
    • Chang Pu (Acorus),
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum),
    • Jie Geng (Platycodon),
    • Fu Ling (Poria),
    • Guan Gui (Cinnamon),
    • Zao Jiao (Soapberry), peeled and roasted,
    • Gan Jiang (Dried ginger), processed,
    • Ren Shen (Ginseng), each 2 taels
    • Huang Lian (Coptis), 2.5 taels
    • Ba Dou (Croton seed) powder, 0.5 taels

    Grind all to a fine powder and mix with Ba Dou powder and honey to form pills about the size of a jujube. Initially take three pills, gradually increasing to five or seven, as a laxative, taken with ginger soup, after meals and while lying down. This medicine's effects are similar to those of the "Wen Bai Wan" from the "Jufang" and is highly effective for diarrhea in late summer and early winter. In spring and summer, add another 2 taels of Huang Lian; in autumn and winter, add another 2 taels of Hou Po.

    San Yi Cheng Qi Tang:

    Ingredients:

    • Dang Gui (Angelica) washed and roasted, 2.5 qian
    • Bei Da Huang (Rhubarb), rough skin removed,
    • Mang Xiao (Glauber's salt),
    • Hou Po (Magnolia bark), ginger-prepared,
    • Zhi Shi (Bitter orange), raw, each 0.5 tael
    • Gan Cao (Licorice), peeled and roasted, 1 tael

    Grind all (as per instructions) and take 0.5 tael per dose with half a water cup; add five slices of ginger and two jujubes split open to decoct for seven minutes, drink hot without straining, regardless of timing. For severe cases, take 1 tael with two extra slices of ginger and one more jujube. If the medicine is not absorbed, sip it frequently to aid passage. Although this is a purgative, it has both purging and supplementing effects, demonstrating remarkable efficacy. Liu Hejian additionally added Gan Cao to create San Yi Cheng Qi, harmonizing the ingredients, best capturing Zhongjing's secret.[106p]

    　　四生丸　治一切结热。常服肢体润泽耐老。　　生芒硝半两　大黄去皮，酒洗纸包煨香不可过　黑牵牛头末　皂角去皮生用，各一两　　右为末，滴水为丸梧桐子大，每服二三十九，白汤送下。
    　　对金饮子
    　　陈皮焙制，八两　苍朮焙　厚朴姜汁炒，各四两　人参　黄芪各一两　黄芩二两半　甘草三两　　右(口父)咀，每服半两，水盏半，生姜五片，枣二枚，同煎七分，去滓热服。先服承气汤，夜服四生丸，如已效进食不格拒，方用对金饮子。然初病作且呕吐，胃热类内选用清利之药，审其虚实重轻，方用前药更佳。[107p]

    Si Sheng Wan treats all types of heat due to accumulation. Regular intake keeps the body moist and resilient to aging.

    Ingredients:

    • Half a tael of raw natron
    • One tael of peeled rhubarb, washed with alcohol, wrapped in paper, and fragrant (not burnt)
    • One tael of black morning glory root powder
    • One tael of peeled soapbark

    Combine these into a powder, then form pills the size of a wutong seed with a little water. Each dose is two to three pills, taken with warm water.

    Dui Jin Yin
    Ingredients:

    • Eight taels of dried tangerine peel
    • Four taels each of roasted atractylodes and thick-fur magnolia bark, fried in ginger juice
    • One tael each of ginseng and astragalus
    • Two and a half taels of scutellaria
    • Three taels of licorice

    Prepare this mixture to a fine powder. Each dose is half a tael, with half a cup of water, five slices of fresh ginger, and two dates, boiled down to seven parts, then strained and served hot.

    Begin with Chengqi Decoction, and take Si Sheng Wan at night. If symptoms worsen and appetite is poor, then use Dui Jin Yin. However, during the initial stages of illness with vomiting and heat in the stomach, use cooling and purging medications, carefully assessing condition to determine suitability of the previous remedies.[107p]

    　　昆布丸 【《良方》，下同】 　治五噎，咽喉妨塞，食饮不下。　　昆布洗去咸水　麦冬去心焙　天冬去心焙　诃黎勒去核，各一两半　木通　川大黄微炒　川(石卜)硝　(木郁)李仁汤浸去皮微炒　肉桂去皮　百合各一两　羚羊角屑　紫苏子　射干　杏仁汤浸去皮尖，麸炒黄，各半两　柴胡去芦　陈皮汤浸去白　槟榔各二钱半　　右为细末，炼蜜和捣三百杵，丸如梧桐子大，每服三十丸，不拘时热酒送下。夜饭后，用绵裹弹子大一丸噙化。
    　　竹皮散　治噎声不出。
    　　竹皮一作竹叶　细辛　通草　人参　五味　茯苓　麻黄　桂心　生姜　甘草各一两　　右(口父)咀，以水一斗，煮竹皮下药，煮取三升，分三服。[108p]

    Kunbu Pill
    For treating five types of choking, obstruction in the throat, and inability to swallow food and drink.
    Wash the kelp to remove the salty water; take one and a half taels each of Ophiopogon (removing the core and roasting), Asparagus (removing the core and roasting), and Myrrh (removing the pit), half a tael each of Akebia, slightly stir-fried Rhubarb, and Potassium Nitrate; take half a tael each of walnut (soaked in broth, skin removed, and slightly stir-fried), Cinnamon (skin removed), Lily, Antelope horn powder, Perilla seeds, Belamcanda, and Bitter Almond (soaked in broth, skin removed, tips cut off, and toasted to yellow); one tael each of Bupleurum (remove the coarse parts) and dried tangerine peel (soaked in broth to remove the white), and two and a half qian each of Areca nut.
    Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, mix with honey, and pound 300 times until shaped into pills the size of a phoenix seed. Take thirty pills each time, with hot wine, without regard to time. After dinner, take one pill the size of a small ball wrapped in cotton and let it dissolve in the mouth.

    Bamboo Skin Powder
    For treating unexpressed choking sounds.
    One tael each of bamboo skin (alternatively bamboo leaves), Asarum, Tongcao, Ginseng, Schisandra, Poria, Ephedra, Cinnamon heart, Ginger, and Licorice.
    Masticate the above ingredients, add ten dou of water, boil with the bamboo skin to obtain three sheng, and divide into three doses.[108p]

    　　吴茱萸丸 【东垣】 　大理脾胃，胸膈不通，调中顺气。　　吴茱萸　草豆蔻各一钱二分　橘皮　益智仁　人参　黄芪　升麻各八分　白僵蚕　泽泻　姜黄　柴胡各四分　当归身　甘草炙，各六分　木香二分　青皮三分　大麦糵一钱五分　半夏一钱　　右为细末，用汤浸蒸饼为丸如菉豆大，每服三十九，细嚼白汤送下。
    　　滋血润肠汤　治血枯及死血在膈，大便燥结。　　当归酒洗，三钱　芍药煨　生地黄各一钱五分　红花酒洗　桃仁去皮尖炒黄　大黄酒煨　枳壳炒，各一钱　　水锺半，煎七分，入韭汁半酒锺，食前服。
    　　人参利膈丸　治血少便燥，膈气之圣药也。　　木香　槟榔各七钱半　人参　藿香　枳实炒　当归酒洗　生甘草各一两　大黄酒蒸透　厚朴姜汁制，各二两　　右为末，水丸桐子大，每服三钱，白汤下。[109p]

    Wu Zhu Yu Wan (Wuzhuyuan): For strengthening the spleen and stomach, and unblocking the chest, regulating the middle and smoothing the qi.
    Ingredients: Wu Zhu Yu and Cao Dou Kou, each 1.2 grams; Ju Pi, Yi Zhi Ren, Ren Shen, Huang Qi, and Sheng Ma, each 0.8 grams; Bai Jiang Can, Ze Xie, Jiang Huang, and Chai Hu, each 0.4 grams; Dang Gui and Zhi Gan Cao, each 0.6 grams; Mu Xiang 0.2 grams; Qing Pi 0.3 grams; Da Mai Miao 1.5 grams; Ban Xia 1 gram.
    Grind to a fine powder, soak with soup and steam into pills the size of mung beans. Take 39 pills, chewing well and wash down with warm water.

    Zi Xue Run Chang Tang: For treating blood deficiency and stagnant blood in the diaphragm, with dry and hard stools.
    Ingredients: Dang Gui, washed with wine, 3 grams; Shao Yao, stewed, and Sheng Di Huang, each 1.5 grams; Hong Hua, washed with wine; Tao Ren, peeled and roasted golden; Da Huang, stewed with wine; Zhi Ke, roasted, each 1 gram.
    Add half a cup of water, decoct to seven-tenths, then mix with half a cup of leek juice and wine, and take before meals.

    Ren Shen Li Ge Wan: For treating insufficient blood and dry stools; a sacred medicine for qi in the diaphragm.
    Ingredients: Mu Xiang and Bing Lang, each 7.5 grams; Ren Shen, Huo Xiang, and Zhi Shi (roasted), Dang Gui (washed with wine), and Sheng Gan Cao, each 30 grams; Da Huang, steamed with wine; Hou Po, prepared with ginger juice, each 30 grams.
    Grind to a powder, form into pills the size of a tung seed. Take 30 grams with warm water.[109p]

    　　进退黄连汤 【喻昌，下同】 　治关格。　　人参人乳拌蒸　半夏姜汁制，各一钱五分　桂枝一钱　大枣二枚　黄连姜汁炒　干姜炮　　进法：用本方七味，俱不制，水三茶锺，煎一半，温服。　　退法：不用桂枝，黄连减半，或加肉桂五分，如上逐味制熟，煎服法同。但空心朝服崔氏八味丸三钱，半饥服煎剂耳。
    　　滋液救焚汤　治五志厥阳之火。
    　　生地黄　麦门冬各二钱，并取汁　胡麻仁炒研　炙甘草　真阿胶　紫石英敲碎　寒水石敲碎　滑石敲碎，各一钱　柏子仁炒，七分　五味四分　生犀三分，研汁　生姜汁二茶匙　　右，除四汁及阿胶共八物，用名山泉水四茶杯，缓火煎至一杯半，去滓，入四汁及阿胶，再上火略煎，至胶烊化斟出，调牛黄细末五厘，日中分二三次热服，空心先服崔氏八味丸三钱。[110p]

    Jin Tui Huang Lian Tang
    For treating barriers.
    Mix and steam ginseng and human milk, each 1.5 qian; ginger juice processed with banxia 1.5 qian; cinnamon branch 1 qian; two jujubes; stir-fry huanglian with ginger juice; and roast dried ginger.
    Method for advancement: Use the seven ingredients above without preparation, boil with three tea cups of water until reduced by half, and take warm.
    Method for retreat: Omit the cinnamon branch, reduce huanglian by half, or add 0.5 qian of cassia. Prepare each ingredient as above, and the boiling method is the same. In the morning on an empty stomach, take 3 qian of Cui's Eight-Flavored Pill, and take the decoction when slightly hungry.

    Zi Ye Jiu Fen Tang
    For treating the fire of the five emotions and the excess yang.
    Fresh Rehmannia and Mai men dong, each 2 qian, extract the juice; stir-fried sesame seeds, roasted licorice, true ejiao, crushed purple quartz, crushed cold water stone, crushed talcum, each 1 qian; stir-fried biota seeds 0.7 qian; five-flavor herb 0.4 qian; fresh rhinoceros horn 0.3 qian, grind for juice; and two teaspoons of fresh ginger juice.
    Aside from the four juices and ejiao, use four tea cups of named mountain spring water, slowly boil until reduced to 1.5 cups, strain, then add the four juices and ejiao, bring to a boil again until the ejiao melts, strain out, mix in 0.5 qian of finely powdered niuhuang, and take hot in two to three doses around midday. Take 3 qian of Cui's Eight-Flavored Pill first on an empty stomach.[110p]

    　　崔氏八味丸
    　　干地黄八两　山茱萸　薯蓣各四两　茯苓　泽泻　牡丹皮各三两　桂枝　附子炮，各一两　　右八味，末之，炼蜜丸梧子大，酒下十五丸，日再。

    　　大补元煎 【《景岳全书》，下同】 　治气血大坏，危剧等证。　　人参少则一二钱，多则一二两　炙甘草一二钱　山茱萸一钱，如畏酸吞酸者去之　山药炒　杜仲各二钱　熟地少则二三钱，多则二三两　当归若泄泻者去之　枸杞各二三钱　　水二锺，煎七分，食远温服。[111p]

    Cui's Eight Ingredients Pill
    Eight ounces of dried rehmannia, four ounces each of cornus and dioscorea, three ounces each of poria, alisma, and peony root, one ounce each of cassia twig and prepared aconite. Grind these eight ingredients, form into pills the size of a walnut, and take fifteen pills with wine, twice a day.

    Returning Yang and Restoring Essence Decoction
    For treating excess Yin counteracting Yang, where Yin is extreme causing restlessness, slight thirst, flushed face, and a desire to sit or lie in muddy water, with a feeble pulse or possibly absent pulse. Use prepared aconite, dried ginger, licorice, ginseng, aged tangerine peel, ophiopogon, schisandra, and for those lacking Yang, add seven stalks of scallion and a little coptis. Boil in one cup of clear muddy water, then add five spoons of honey before taking cold to induce sweating.

    Great Supplementing Original Decoction
    For treating severe damages to Qi and Blood, and critical complications. Use ginseng (one or two qian if less, or one or two liang if more), roasted licorice (one or two qian), one qian of cornus (omit if craving acidity), stir-fried dioscorea and eucommia (two qian each), dried rehmannia (two or three qian if less, or two or three liang if more), omit angelica if there is diarrhea, and goji berries (two or three qian). Use two cups of water; boil down to seven parts, and take warm away from meals.[111p]

    Zuo Gui Decoction: For those with the yin of the life gate weakened and yang strong, this is suitable. Use 2 to 3 qian of cooked rehmannia, and may add up to 1 or 2 liang; 1.5 qian of poria; 2 qian each of chinese yam and goji berries; 1 to 2 qian of cornelian cherry (reduce if sensitive to sour); 1 qian of honey-fried licorice. Use 2 zhong of water, decoct to 7 portions, and take on an empty stomach.

    You Gui Decoction: For those with the yang of the life gate weakened and yin strong, this is suitable. Use cooked rehmannia as before; 2 qian each of chinese yam, goji berries, and cooked eucommia with ginger; 1 to 2 to 3 qian of prepared aconite; 1 qian of cornelian cherry; 1 to 2 qian each of honey-fried licorice and cinnamon. Use 2 zhong of water, decoct to 7 portions, and take warm on an empty stomach.

    Zuo Gui Pill: Treats insufficient true yin, depletion of essence and marrow, and dryness of fluids. Use 8 liang of large-harvest cooked rehmannia; 3 liang of steamed, wine-washed, and well-sifted chinese ligustrum; 4 liang each of dried chinese yam, cornelian cherry flesh, crushed and fried deer glue, goji berries, and prepared dodder seeds, and cut shredded turtle glue. Those without fire do not need to use. First, stew the cooked rehmannia until mushy, then mix in honey to form pills the size of a tung seed, taking over a hundred pills with boiling water or lightly salted soup before meals.[112p]

    　　右归丸　治元阳不足，命门火衰，而为翻胃噎膈等证。　　大怀熟地八两　山茱萸微炒　当归各三两，便溏勿用　制附子自二两渐可加至五六两　枸杞子微炒　鹿角胶炒珠　菟丝子制　杜仲姜汁炒断丝　山药炒，各四两　肉桂二两，渐可加至四两　　右丸法如前，或丸如弹子大，每嚼服二三丸，以滚白汤送下，其效尤速。
    　　五福饮　治五脏气血亏损者。

    You Gui Wan treats the insufficiency of the original yang, diminished fire at the Mingmen, resulting in symptoms such as reversed stomach and esophageal obstruction. Ingredients include:

    • 8 taels of cooked rehmannia
    • lightly toasted shanzhuyu: 3 taels
    • each of danggui: 3 taels (do not use if too loose)
    • prepared fuzi: start with 2 taels, gradually increase to 5 or 6 taels
    • lightly toasted goji berries: 3 taels
    • toasted deer antler glue pearls: 3 taels
    • prepared cuscus: 3 taels
    • zhi du zhong with ginger juice: 3 taels, toasted until broken strands
    • toasted yam: 3 taels
    • cinnamon: start with 2 taels, gradually increase to 4 taels

    The method for making the pills is as stated above, or roll into the size of a marble. Chew and take 2 or 3 pills with warm white soup; its effects are particularly swift.

    Wu Fu Drink treats deficiencies in the qi and blood of the five organs.

    • Ginseng and cooked rehmannia: as needed
    • Danggui: 2 or 3 qian
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1 qian
    • Fried baizhu: 1.5 qian

    Use 2 sheng of water to decoct to 7 parts, and take it warm after meals.

    Yi Yin Jiao treats yin deficiency with predominant yang symptoms, excessive fire causing heat and blood movement.

    • Cooked rehmannia: 3 to 5 qian
    • Niu xi: 1.5 qian
    • Licorice: 1 qian
    • Fresh rehmannia
    • Shao yao
    • Mai dong
    • Dan shen: each 2 qian

    Use 2 sheng of water to decoct to 7 parts, and take it warm after meals.

    San Yin Jiao treats liver and spleen deficiency, insufficient essence and blood.

    • Ginseng: as needed
    • Danggui: 2 or 3 qian
    • Cooked rehmannia: 3 to 5 qian
    • Sour jujube seed and shaoyao, fried in wine: each 2 qian
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1 qian

    Use 2 sheng of water to decoct to 7 parts, and take it warm after meals.[113p]

    Da Ying Jian: Used for treating true yin deficiency, qi and blood deficiency, and cold symptoms.
    Ingredients: 2 to 3 qian or 5 qian of Angelica sinensis, 3 to 5 to 7 qian of Rehmannia, 2 qian each of Goji berry and Eucommia bark, 1.5 qian of Achyranthes, 1 to 2 qian each of cinnamon and honey-fried licorice.
    Method: Boil with 2 zhong of water until reduced to 7 parts, take warm after meals.

    Jin Shui Liu Jun Jian: Used for treating lung and kidney deficiency with cold, fluid retention manifesting as phlegm, or symptoms of yin deficiency with insufficient blood and qi.
    Ingredients: 3 to 5 qian of Rehmannia, 1.5 qian of dried tangerine peel, 1 qian of honey-fried licorice, 2 qian each of Angelica sinensis, Pinellia ternata, and Poria.
    Method: Boil with 2 zhong of water and 3 to 5 to 7 slices of fresh ginger until reduced to 7 or 8 parts, take warm after meals.

    Liu An Jian: Used for treating phlegm obstruction and qi reversal.
    Ingredients: 1.5 qian of dried tangerine peel, 2 to 3 qian of Pinellia ternata, 2 qian of Poria, 1 qian each of licorice and peeled apricot kernel, 5 to 7 fen of white mustard seed (omit for the elderly with weak qi).
    Method: Boil with 1.5 zhong of water, adding 3 to 5 to 7 slices of fresh ginger until reduced to 7 parts, take away from meals.

    Shao Yao Zhi Zhu Wan: Used for treating food stagnation with distention and fullness.
    Ingredients: 2 liang each of fried Atractylodes and red peony, 1 liang each of fried bitter orange and dried tangerine peel.
    Method: Cook with lotus leaf tea to make a paste for walnut-sized pills, take with rice drink or boiling water as desired, up to more than 100 pills.[114p]

    　　神香散　治逆气痰饮膈噎，诸药不效者。　　丁香　白豆蔻或砂仁亦可二味等分为末，清汤调下五七分，甚者一钱，日数服，不拘。

    　　五君子煎　治前证。
    　　人参二三钱　干姜炒黄，一二钱　炙甘草一钱　白朮　茯苓各二钱　　水一锺半，煎服。[115p]

    Divine Fragrance Powder: Treats counteracting qi, phlegm, and obstruction in the diaphragm; for those where other medicines are ineffective. Use cloves and white cardamom or sand ginger, equally divided into a powder, mixed with clear broth, taken in doses of five to seven fen (grams), with severe cases one qian (3 grams), taken multiple times a day, as needed.

    Four-Material Yang-Recovery Decoction: Treats sudden yang deficiency and imminent danger. Ingredients: one to two liang (31-62 grams) of ginseng, one to two qian (3-6 grams) of roasted licorice, fuzi (prepared aconite) peeled, and dry ginger, each two to three qian. Combine with two sheng (0.5 liters) of water, boil vigorously until reduced to seven or eight portions, take warm, sipping gradually.

    Six-Material Yang-Recovery Decoction: Treats symptoms of impending yin and yang collapse. Ingredients: one to two liang of ginseng or several qian, one qian of roasted licorice, prepared fuzi, and dry ginger, each two to three qian; three qian of the body of angelica (Dang Gui); if diarrhea or blood movement occurs, substitute with winter wormwood; five qian or one liang of cooked rehmannia. Combine with two sheng of water, boil vigorously until reduced to seven or eight portions, take warm.

    Warm Stomach Decoction: Treats middle cold, vomiting after eating, and diaphragm obstruction. Ingredients: one to three qian or one liang of ginseng, one to two qian or one liang of roasted white atractylodes, two qian of roasted broad beans, one to three qian of burnt dry ginger, one qian of roasted licorice, and aged tangerine peel (optional); one to two qian of angelica (avoid for those with diarrhea). Combine with two sheng of water, boil until reduced to seven portions, take warm away from meals.

    Five Gentlemen Decoction: Treats the aforementioned symptoms. Ingredients: two to three qian of ginseng, one to two qian of roasted yellow dry ginger, one qian of roasted licorice, and two qian each of white atractylodes and poria. Combine with one and a half sheng of water, decoct to consume.[115p]

    　　黄芽丸　治前证。
    　　人参二两　焦干姜三钱
    　　右，炼白蜜为丸芡实大，常嚼服之。
    　　圣朮煎　治寒湿反胃。
    　　陈皮酌用　冬朮炒，五六钱或一二两　肉桂　干姜炒，各一二钱　　水一锺半，煎七分，温热服。

    　　豕膏　治噎膈。
    　　当归半斤，浓煎取汁　猪脂炼过，一斤　　右二味同炼，去其水气，乃入白蜜一斤，再炼少顷，滤凈收贮，不时挑服。用治老人之秘结及噎膈闭结等证，必妙。如果阳气不行者，仍加生姜四两，同当归煎入，或宜酒者，以酒送服亦可。或气有不利者，加杏仁二两去皮尖，同前煎入皆妙。或有滞者，当以饧代蜜，更妙。是即《内经》所谓以辛润之也。
    　　　　单方

    　　凡男妇翻胃吐食，白垩土煅赤，以米酢一升淬之，再煅再淬，酢干为度，取一两研，干姜二钱半，炮为末，每服一钱调下，服至一斤以上为妙。【《千金》】[116p]

    Huang Ya Wan: Treats pre-existing symptoms.
    Two taels of ginseng, three qian of roasted dried ginger.
    Prepare these into pills the size of a millet. Chew and consume regularly.

    Sheng Zhu Jian: Treats cold-dampness causing stomach reversal.
    Use aged tangerine peel as needed, five or six qian of winter ginseng, or one to two taels, and one to two qian of cinnamon and roasted dried ginger. Boil with one and a half sheng of water until reduced by seven parts, consume warm.

    Pig Oil: Treats esophageal obstruction.
    Half a jin of angelica, concentrated and juiced, and a jin of processed pig fat. Mix these two ingredients well, remove moisture, and add one jin of white honey. Refine briefly, filter clean, and store for occasional consumption. It is used to treat elderly patients with secretive blockages and throat obstructions, very effective. If yang energy is deficient, add four taels of fresh ginger and cook with the angelica, or if better with wine, it can also be taken with wine. If there are adverse energies, add two taels of blanched almonds and cook them together. If there are stagnations, use syrup instead of honey for even better results. This corresponds to what is known as "moisten with pungent substances" in the Inner Canon.

    Simple Recipe:
    For all men and women with reversed stomach and vomiting, calcine white clay until red, then soak in one sheng of rice vinegar. Repeat calcining and soaking until the vinegar is dry. Take one tael, grind it, and mix with two and a half qian of dried ginger, making a powder. Take one qian each time, mix and swallow, consuming over one jin for best results. [116p]

    　　又反胃转食，用地龙屎一两，木香三钱，大黄七钱为末，每服五钱，无根水调服。忌煎煿、酒酢、椒姜热物，其效如神。【《经验方》】　　又方：取螺蛳一斗，水浸取泥晒干，每服一钱，火酒调下。　　又方：取灶中土五年久者为末，米饮服三钱，经验。 【《百一》】
    　　反胃吐食：用梁上倒挂尘，黑驴尿调服之。 【《集简方》】
    　　反胃哕逆：黑铅化汁，以柳木槌研成粉一两，入米酢一升，砂锅熬膏，入蒸饼末少许捣丸菉豆大，每服一丸姜汤下。【《圣济》，下同】
    　　多年反胃不止：紫背铅二两，烧铅，以盐卤汁五两焠尽，与石亭脂二两，同炒焰起，挑水于上，焰止，研匀，蒸饼丸梧子大，每服二十丸，煎石莲干柿汤下。
    　　吐逆不止：宜用碧霞丹。用北黄丹四两，米酢半升煎干，炭火三秤，就铫内煅红，冷定为末，粟米饭丸梧子大，每服七丸，酢汤下。【《集验方》】[117p]

    For nausea and vomiting of food: Use one tael of earthworm excrement, three qian of costus, and seven qian of rhubarb, ground into a powder. Take five qian each time, mixed with water without roots. Avoid fried, hot, or spicy foods; its effect is miraculous.

    Another prescription: Take one dou (about 10 liters) of river snails, soak in water, extract mud, and dry. Take one qian each time, mixed with fire wine.

    Another prescription: Use five-year-old soil from the stove, ground into powder; take three qian with rice drink, according to experience.

    For recurrent nausea and vomiting: Use dust hanging from the beam, mixed with black donkey urine to take.

    For nausea and regurgitation: Use black lead juice, ground into powder with a willow wood pestle, one tael. Mix with one liter of rice vinegar, boil in a sandy pot to make a paste, then mix with a small amount of steamed cake powder to form pills the size of mung beans, taking one pill with ginger soup.

    For prolonged nausea that doesn't stop: Use two taels of purple back lead, burn the lead, quench with five taels of brine, and stir with two taels of stone gall. When the flames rise, pour water on top, stop the flames, grind evenly, and make pills the size of walnuts from steamed cake. Take twenty pills each time with an infusion of dried lotus stone and persimmons.

    For persistent regurgitation: It is advisable to use Bixia Dan. Use four taels of northern yellow lead, boil with half a liter of rice vinegar until dry, then measure three scales of charcoal fire to red-hot, and grind into powder once cooled. Make pills the size of walnuts from millet rice; take seven pills each time with vinegar soup.[117p]

    　　胃虚反胃气逆：鉛丹二两，白矾二两，生熟亭脂半两，以丹矾研匀入坩锅内，以炭半升煅赤，更养一夜，出毒两日，入亭脂同研，粟米饭和丸菉豆大，每日米饮下十五丸。【《圣济》，下同】
    　　反胃吐食水不能停：黑铅、水银各一钱半，结砂舶硫黄五钱，官桂一钱，为末，每服六钱，一半米汤，一半自然姜汁调，作一处服。
    　　脾痛反胃：灵砂一两、蚌粉一两同炒，赤丁香、胡椒各四十九粒为末，自然姜汁，煮半夏粉糊丸梧子大，每姜汤下二十丸。【《普济》】
    　　反胃吐食：雄黄一分、甘草生半分为末，饭丸梧子大，以五叶草糯米煎汤，每服四丸。【《圣济》】
    　　反胃吐食绝好：赤石脂为末，蜜丸梧子大，每空腹姜汤下一二十丸。先以巴豆仁一枚，勿令破，以津吞之，后乃服药。【《圣惠》】[118p]

    Stomach deficiency causing regurgitation: Two taels of lead sulfide, two taels of alum, half a tael of raw and cooked tallow. Grind the lead and alum evenly and place them in a crucible; calcine with half a sheng of charcoal until red, then let it rest for a night to expel toxins for two days. Mix in the tallow and grind together. Make pills the size of millet beans from rice porridge, taking fifteen pills daily.

    For spleen pain causing regurgitation: One tael of spirit sand and one tael of clam powder are stir-fried together, with forty-nine grains each of clove and pepper ground to powder. Mix with ginger juice, make into pills the size of walnuts, taking twenty pills with ginger soup.

    For regurgitation and vomiting food: One fen of realgar and half a fen of raw licorice are ground into powder, made into pills the size of walnuts, taken with a decoction of five-leafed clover glutinous rice, taking four pills each time.

    For excellent results with regurgitation and vomiting food: Grind red stone resin into powder, make into honey pills the size of walnuts, and take one or twenty pills before meals with ginger soup. First swallow one unbroken seed of hyacinth bean with saliva, then take the medicine.[118p]

    　　痰饮吐水无时节者，其原因冷饮过度，遂令脾胃气弱，不能消化饮食，饮食入胃，皆变成冷水，反吐不停，赤石脂散主之。赤石脂一斤，捣筛服方寸匕，酒饮自任，稍加至三匕。服尽一斤，则终身不吐痰水，又不下利。补五脏，令人肥健。有人痰饮服诸药不效，服此遂愈。【《千金翼》】
    　　噎膈反胃：用北庭砂二钱，水和荞麦面包之，煅焦待冷，取中间湿者焙干一宿，入槟榔二钱、丁香二个研匀，每服七厘，烧酒送下，日三服，愈即止，后吃白粥半月，仍服助胃丸药。　　又方：以北庭砂一两，人言末一两，同入罐内，文武火升三炷，取出灯盞上末一两，以黄丹末一两，同入罐内，如上法升之；取末用桑灰霜一两，研匀，每服三分，烧酒下，愈即止。　　又方：用平胃散各一钱，入硇砂、生姜各五分为末，沸汤点服二钱，当吐出黑物如石，屡验。[119p]

    If phlegm and water are vomited without seasonal cause, the reason is excessive consumption of cold drinks, which weakens the spleen and stomach Qi, making it unable to digest food. Food enters the stomach and transforms into cold water, leading to persistent vomiting. The remedy is red stone resin. Take one pound of red stone resin, crush and sift it, and take a small amount with wine, gradually increasing to three spoonfuls. If one pound is completely consumed, one will not vomit phlegm or have diarrhea for life. It nourishes the five organs and promotes health. Some people fail to be cured by other medicines for phlegm, but this remedy proves effective.

    For choking and reverse stomach flow: Use two qian of Northern Courtyard Sand, mix it with buckwheat flour, and calcine it until charred; let it cool and take the moist center, drying it overnight. Add two qian of areca nut and two cloves, grind them together, and take seven li, washed down with liquor, three times daily, stopping once cured. Afterwards, eat plain congee for half a month and continue taking stomach-consolidating pills.

    Another method: Take one liang of Northern Courtyard Sand; some say one liang of the powder. Combine it with one liang of yellow lead powder and heat as before; use one liang of mulberry ash powder, grind well, and take three fen, washed down with liquor, stopping once cured.

    Another method: Take one qian of Pingwei San, and mix with half a qian each of sand and fresh ginger to make a powder; use boiling water to prepare two qian, and one will expel black substances like stones, regularly effective.[119p]

    　　反胃呕吐不止：用干钖糖六两，生姜四两，二味同捣作饼，或焙或晒，入炙甘草末二两，盐少许，点汤服之。常熟一富人病反胃，往京口甘露寺设水陆，泊舟岸下，梦一僧持汤一杯与之，饮罢，便觉胸快。次早入寺，供汤者乃梦中所见僧。常以此汤待宾，故易名甘露汤。能利胸膈，养脾胃，进饮食。[124p]

    Difficulty swallowing food: For this, take red rice with fine sprouts, burn to ash, and prepare a broth by straining through silk three times. Combine the broth with one clove of clove, half a seed of cardamom, and a cup of rice to make porridge. It is highly effective.

    Nausea and vomiting: Use poppy seed porridge. Take three measures of white poppy seeds, three large coins of ginseng powder, and five inches of yam, finely chopped and ground. Combine these with two and a half liters of water, boil down to six proportions, add a bit of fresh ginger juice and salt, mix well, and take divided doses without concern for timing; it is also fine to take it in powdered form with medicinal pills.

    Nausea with obstructed qi preventing food intake: Use Taicang powder. Take barnyard millet or white rice, moisten it lightly with water in the late afternoon, envisioning the day's heat entering the rice. The next day, dry it in the sun, store in a bag and hang in the wind, taking a pinch to brew in water, drink it, and it will be effective immediately. Another recipe: Cook aged barnyard millet, grind it, and for every 250 grams, mix in 15 grams of agarwood powder, combine well, and take two or three coins of the mixture with a drink.

    Persistent nausea and vomiting: Use six taels of dried ginger sugar and four taels of fresh ginger, pound them into a cake, either bake or sun-dry, then add two taels of roasted licorice powder and a little salt, take with broth. A wealthy man from Changshu had nausea, went to Jingkou's Ganlu Temple for water and land offerings, and dreamt of a monk giving him a cup of broth; after drinking, he felt relief in his chest. The next morning, he found that the one who served the broth was the monk from his dream. Since this broth was often used to entertain guests, it was renamed Ganlu Broth. It effectively benefits the chest, nourishes the spleen and stomach, and promotes appetite.[124p]

    1. For food obstruction: Grind pigweed and white cardamom into powder, then dry and lick it.

    Nausea and Vomiting:
    Use the shells of yellow clams and paddy snails, taking equal parts that have been in the mud for a long time, fry them into white ash. For every four ounces, add four pieces of white plum meat, pound them together into balls, then put them in a sand box, cover with mud to set, calcine to preserve potency, grind into a fine powder. Take two qian each time, mixed with ginseng decoction to drink. Alternatively, it can also be taken with old rice drink. Whenever there is a feeling of bloating and pain in the abdomen leading to nausea, use this medicine to treat it.

    Nausea and Stagnation of Qi:
    Take seven geckos, fry them until charred in a sand pot, and add 1.5 qian each of costus, ginseng, and cinnabar, and 1 qian of frankincense ground into powder, making pills the size of a nut. Take seven pills each time, with a decoction of costus, morning and evening.

    Nausea and Vomiting:
    Burn hedgehog skin into ash to drink with wine, or boil it into juice, or try five flavors with roasted food.

    Nausea and Vomiting:
    Take one large crucian carp, remove its intestines but leave the scales, fill it with powdered green vitriol until packed, calcine to preserve potency, and grind into powder. Each time, take one qian with rice drink, twice daily.

    Stagnation of Qi and Vomiting:
    With a large crucian carp, remove its intestines but keep the scales, stuff it with slices of garlic, wrap it in ten layers of paper, seal with mud, and dry partially in the sun. Cook it over charcoal until done, remove the skin and take the flesh, mix it with one liang of Pingwei powder, make into pills the size of a nut, and store them securely. Each time, take thirty pills, to be swallowed with rice drink.[128p]

    A skilled woman knows remedies for obstructed digestion and choking ailments, using a piece of burned ash with wine or a dose of three qian, yielding remarkable results.

    For choking and reversed stomach, when various medicines fail: one qian of true asafoetida and three qian of dried human feces from the wild, prepared with ginger juice, can revive the dead. This is a recipe from King Zhao's collection.
